albatross

by 324b2fun

Summary

In a grab for political power, Rio finds herself in an arranged marriage with the heir to the Harkness Empire. Resigned to her duties as a filial daughter, Rio believes she will be able to swallow her pride and live in a loveless marriage for the rest of her life.

That is until she meets her soon-to-be sister-in-law, the black sheep of the family, Agatha.

Notes

a fun fact and explanation for the title of this fic: it’s an allusion to the poem the rime of the ancient mariner, where after killing an albatross (a bird), a ship captain is forced to wear it around his neck as a symbol of shame and guilt due to the misfortune the killing of an innocent brought upon his crew

i ended up going with this bc it matched the plot and themes of the fics so yeah!! i will end my nerdy rambling here

enjoy!!

Chapter 1

Chapter Summary

An engagement becomes official.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

If there was one thing Rio was ever taught by her parents, it was to put her family above all else. 

It was an easy thing to follow when she was younger. A missed birthday here, a college decision there. Everything she did, Rio believed it was for the best, both for herself and her family. That was what you were supposed to do. That was what it meant to be a good daughter.

Rio never questioned this philosophy until now. 

As Rio stared out the car window, there was a heaviness in the air that only worsened her anxiety. Out of a habit, she lifted a hand to gnaw on the nail of her thumb. The finger barely brushed her lips before her mother, Paola, slapped it away. Rio flinched and pressed her hands to her thighs. She didn’t need to look at her mother to see the admonishing look on her face.

“Remember,” Luis said, “All you have to do is smile.”

Luis Vidal used to be Rio’s hero. Growing up, Rio used to follow her father around whenever she could, awed by the way he commanded a room and persuaded others to follow his lead. It was like having a super power in her eyes, this ability to make things happen the way Luis seemed to do. When Rio asked her father how he managed to do this, he sat her in front of a chessboard.

Luis was merciless in the way he taught her chess, but Rio only worked harder to meet her father’s expectations. As they played together, Luis explained how every meeting he had was like a game of chess. He winked at her and said, “It’s all about strategy. You just have to know your opponent’s next move.”

Now, at the age of twenty-nine, Rio found herself one step behind her father, a helpless pawn set out for the sacrifice.

“It’ll be okay,” Paola told her. She placed her hand over Rio’s before she could start picking at them. “They’re a good family.” Paola’s laugh was forced and light. “But you know that.”

Making small talk over a glass of champagne was much different than marriage, Rio wanted to point out. Instead, she gave a wan smile and kept her eyes firmly on the window.

Far too quickly, they arrived at the Harkness Estate, a sprawling piece of land in Upstate New York. Although Rio had grown up privileged, she felt the enormity of the wealth that came with being the bloodline of old money. Rio stepped out of the car and eyed the looming house with trepidation. Calling it a house felt like an understatement. Rio had seen museums smaller than this.

Rio followed her parents to the door, where they were greeted by a maid who ushered them inside and took their coats. As she glanced around, she took note of the decor. Antiques littered the tables and walls, and Rio had no doubt that each one was at least a few centuries old. None of them were ugly at least, but Rio always wondered what the point of collecting such expensive, useless items was. 

“Our honored guests! How lovely it is to see you again.”

Rio stiffened, but she still turned to greet their host with a smile. She held out her arms and accepted the brief hug Evanora swept her into, barely refraining from flinching as Evanora’s breath ghosted against her cheek as a kiss. 

“Rio, you are still absolutely stunning,” Evanora said. She squeezed her arms and added, “Goodness, I see the summer sun has been kind to you. You look positively exotic.”

The smile nearly dropped off Rio’s face, but she managed to hold onto it. Rio’s voice was remarkably even as she answered, “Thank you, Mrs. Harkness.”

“Evanora. We’ll be family soon.”

“Of course. Evanora.”

They were led into the sitting room, and while her parents joined Evanora on the couch and the armchairs, Rio took a deep breath as she met James where he stood by the window. 

It hadn’t been that long since she last saw him at an event, and James looked just the same as he always had. Objectively, he was handsome with round, brown eyes, a square jaw, and neatly styled brown hair. Rio didn’t feel an ounce of attraction towards him though. Not even as he leaned in and gave her a hug, letting his hands rest firm against her back.

“Rio,” James said warmly. “I hope the drive wasn’t too arduous.”

“Not at all,” Rio replied. She smiled, trying to match his ease. “Thank you for inviting us. Your home is beautiful.”

This, at least, Rio could handle. There was a kind of small talk Rio could do in her sleep, and that was all that was required of her so far. A simple cycle of compliments and catch-ups, never dipping into anything more than carefully feigned interest.

When a maid slipped into the room and whispered into Evanora’s ear, the woman stood up and announced, “I hope you’re starved. I had my chef prepare a special set of courses for us tonight.”

Rio started to move when Luis said, “Is your daughter not joining us?” He had an eyebrow raised in an expression Rio was well accustomed to. “I was under the impression this was a family affair.” 

Evanora’s smile became strained as she said, “Unfortunately, Agatha lives by her own schedule. She will join us when she joins us.”

Rio caught a glimpse of dismay cross her father’s face, and when she glanced at James, she saw a similar expression. When he caught her looking though, James schooled his face into a charming grin and guided her to the dining room. 

The reactions made Rio curious. Of course, Rio had heard of Agatha before. Everyone knew about Agatha Harkness, the black sheep of her family. The youngest daughter of the Harknesses, Agatha had always been at the center of any discourse. In the beginning, it was of her potential. Stunning in a way that was almost aristocratic, quick thinking in every subject, and practically a prodigy at the cello. Destined for greatness.

Then, Agatha had rebelled.

Three years her junior, Rio had only been eleven when she first heard news of Agatha’s transformation from socialite darling to family embarrassment. It was only rumors, but Rio heard it all, the sex and drugs and run-ins with the law. 

It became clear that Agatha Harkness was not fit for the world she’d been born into. Too rough around the edges. Too willing to cross the lines. Too curious for her own good. Too much of everything, apparently. 

Rio had always wondered how it must feel to live like that. To disappoint everyone who loved you. But also, to be free.

Everyone had just taken their seats when the front door opened, followed by the giggles of one of the maids. If Evanora’s smile had been strained before, it was brittle now. One move away from shattering her shiny facade.

“Speak of the devil,” Evanora said. She inclined her head to a spot behind Rio. “Agatha.”

“Sorry, Mother. You know how traffic is.”

The voice was low, but the tone was flippant. Rio felt a shiver pass through her at the sound. A hand brushed against the back of her chair before Agatha passed by, falling into Rio’s line of sight.

Agatha, Rio noted, must take after their late father. She was nothing but sharp features, something that was only further emphasized by her long, dark hair against pale skin and bright blue eyes. Agatha was beautiful, just as the rumors always said. Unlike the dresses Rio and the other woman wore, Agatha wore a tailored suit like the men, complete with a maroon tie that matched the color painting her lips. 

Agatha’s eyes felt too intense as they landed on her. With a slight curl of her lips, Agatha said, “And you must be the bride-to-be.”

“It’s a pleasure to meet you,” Rio said. A blush spread across her cheeks, one that only worsened as Agatha’s smile grew. 

Agatha sat down in the only seat left, right across from Rio. It made sense, in a way. Evanora and Paola sat across from each other, as did James and Luis. Why would it be odd from Rio to sit across from her future sister-in-law?

Despite telling herself this, Rio felt out of sorts all throughout dinner. She could hardly taste the food that was placed in front of her, eating it robotically. Every time she tried to follow along with the conversation, she felt her eyes drawn back to Agatha, who made no effort to hide her stare. 

“Why were you late?” Rio finally asked. Beside her, Luis was asking James about a meeting he’d had with a city council member recently. Rio couldn’t have cared less. She had to say something to someone though, or else she’d go mad with the way Agatha’s eyes seemed to be burning into her.

For a moment, Agatha looked surprised to have been asked a question, but then she picked up her wine glass and gave it a contemplative swirl. “Traffic. Didn’t you hear?”

Rio almost laughed. She kept her voice quiet as she said, “We both know there was no traffic.”

“My, my, are you trying to imply something?” Agatha said. There was no actual offense in her voice. Amusement, more than anything. She rested her chin on her hand and tilted her head at Rio, a thread of condescension to the action that made Rio bristle. “I mean, as eager as I was to meet my brother’s fiancée, I do have a life.”

“Which was it, drawing up the papers for someone’s divorce or kicking another woman out of your brownstone?” Rio said without thinking. She hadn’t meant to mention the tawdry details included in the rumors surrounding Agatha. She held her breath, waiting for the yelling, but Agatha only looked like she was holding back a laugh.

Agatha’s pout was nothing but mocking as she said, “Aw, is someone jealous of my job?” She smirked and leaned in, “Or maybe my sex life?”

“I’m a doctor,” Rio hissed.

“Not for long,” Agatha said without missing a beat. “And I don’t hear any denial about the sex.”

Rio’s hand tightened around her knife, but before she could do much more than that, James asked her for her opinion on locations for the honeymoon. Rio tried to deflect, letting her mind process the back-and-forth that had just happened. Her hands were clammy, and her heart was beating just a bit faster than normal. 

It wasn’t normal for Rio to not get along with others. Even at work, Rio usually ended up with the most prickly of nurses because her more easy-going attitude made things run smoothly. There was just something about Agatha though, something that made Rio’s walls go up and pushed her to attack first. Rio didn’t want to think of a conversation where Agatha had the upper hand. Or, more of an upper hand.

As dinner continued, Rio was included in more of the conversations, leaving her to pretend to care about what kind of napkins would be used at the reception and how she might style her hair for the wedding. It wasn’t until dessert was served that Rio felt something brush her ankle. She nearly fell out of her chair from startling so badly. While everyone asked if she was okay, Rio found her gaze drawn to Agatha, the one person to not look surprised. Rio knew she hadn’t imagined it, a pointed heel against her leg. 

“I’m fine,” Rio said. She forced a clumsy laugh and said, “I think my foot fell asleep.”

James wore an indulgent smile, but Rio saw the disapproval in her father’s eyes. When she looked away, she was met with Agatha’s smile, a knowing edge to it that made Rio want to bolt. 

Agatha didn’t try anything else during the meal, but when their families said good-bye, her hug was far tighter than courtesy required with her hands lingering on Rio’s hips and back. “Until next time,” Agatha whispered in her ear.

Rio couldn’t get out of that house fast enough.

It wasn’t until she was in the car, heading back into the city, that Rio let herself relax. Of course, that didn’t last for very long. A few minutes into the drive, Paola said, “I think that went well, don’t you?”

Rio said nothing, thinking she was talking to her father, but when the silence went on too long, she looked away from the window to find both of her parents looking at her expectantly. “It was fine,” Rio said. She lifted her hand to her mouth, and this time, Paola did not stop her as Rio bit at her thumb nail.

“Don’t be like that,” Paola sighed. “You could be a little more excited, you know. You’re getting married, Rio.”

“Exciting, isn’t it?” Luis chimed in. He reached out and tugged Rio’s hand away from her mouth, clutching it in his own. “My little girl is getting married in just one month.”

Rio only smiled and let her hand eventually fall from his grip. The conversation shifted away from her, and Rio was left to stare out the window once more.

It’d been three weeks since Rio found out about this marriage. It’d been two weeks since Rio accepted it. It’d been one week since Rio received a diamond ring that fit her perfectly, delivered by courier with a handwritten note from James.

It’d been fifteen years since Rio knew she was a lesbian.

And that was the crux of it all. It didn’t matter how kind or thoughtful or handsome James was. It would never matter. This, Rio could have lived with. A loveless marriage to a man who could have been worse. 

But then, there just had to be Agatha, an infuriating woman that made Rio’s unfortunate situation even worse. Yet even as she rankled Rio’s nerves and made her want to crawl out of her skin to avoid her gaze, she would always be infinitely more attractive, more interesting , to Rio than James. And she was, both attractive and interesting, no matter how much Rio loathed her at the same time.

Rio had thought she had more time to deal with the fact that she’d never have what she desired most, but now, it was just one month. 

One month. That was how long Rio had to reconcile the fact that for the rest of her life she would want her sister-in-law in ways she would never want her husband.

Chapter 2

Chapter Summary

Rio goes wedding dress shopping. It could've gone worse. (It also could've gone a lot better.)

If there was one thing Rio was going to miss when she inevitably moved, it would be her garden.

Rio wasn’t sure if garden was an exaggeration for the handful of planters and pots scattered around her balcony, but she loved it all the same. Whenever she came out here, watering and tending to her plants, Rio got a few minutes of peace, a few minutes to breathe. It was easily her favorite part of the day.

Would it be possible to take her plants with her? Would James allow that?

Immediately, Rio cringed at her own thoughts. Allow. Like she was some naive child begging to bring a stray dog home, instead of a grown woman wanting to take her belongings with her once she was married. 

Rio reached underneath one of the chairs on her balcony, digging through a dirty blanket until she found a plastic bag. Inside was a half-filled carton of cigarettes and a lighter. This was the one thing Rio had done in her youth that would have even remotely qualified as rebellious, and it was a habit that had stuck with her through the years. While she didn’t smoke nearly as much as she had in college, Rio still found herself reaching for it whenever she was particularly stressed or upset. 

Leaning against the railing, Rio looked out at the city beneath her and sighed. 

What the hell had she gotten herself into?

Rio was contemplating this question when her doorbell rang. Knowing who it was, she didn’t bother to put out her cigarette as she went to answer the door. Alice looked unsurprised to see it in her hand, but she still said, “That bad?”

“I’m marrying a man,” Rio replied, stepping back to let her in. “What do you think?”

“I think you should be day drinking, not smoking, but what do I know?” Alice said with a shrug. She checked her phone and asked, “Should we go ahead and leave now?”

Rio took another drag from her cigarette. There was an appointment at ten to look at wedding dresses. It was the kind of thing that should evoke a sense of excitement, not an ever-increasing dread. Rio’s lack of enthusiasm had been palpable over the phone last week, so as a show of good will, Paola encouraged her to invite Alice, her longtime friend from college. Really, the only person Rio talked to outside of family these days. 

“Might as well,” Rio said. “Let me grab my coat.”

To kill a bit of time, not to mention dispel some of the smell of smoke clinging to her, Rio and Alice walked to the boutique where Rio was sure her dress would cost as much as a small car. As they walked, Rio caught Alice up on the details of her impending marriage.

“At least he’s not a total stranger,” Alice reasoned. 

“Not a stranger but not a friend either,” Rio said. “Not that it really matters in a political marriage.”

Alice bumped her shoulder against Rio’s. “And his views?”

“Could be worse.”

“As in?”

Rio shrugged, “Not a complete idiot, but he’s definitely more traditional.”

“So it’s like that,” Alice said with a wince. She shoved her hands deeper into the pockets of her jacket. “But he treats you okay?”

Rio exhaled sharply through her nose. Not quite a laugh but amused all the same. “Alice, I haven’t spoken to him for more than ten minutes, and it’s never been alone,” Rio said.

“Some guys are pretty fucking awful from the start,” Alice pointed out. Her eyebrows were drawn together, and her voice dropped into a grumble. “Forgive me for checking to see if he’s one of them.” Her lips were twisted into a frown, and Rio noticed just how tense her shoulders were. She was reminded that she wasn’t the only one unhappy about this arrangement. 

“Sorry,” Rio murmured. “I just don’t like thinking about how little I know about him. About all of this.”

Alice didn’t say anything at first. They walked in silence for a minute or two, arms brushing as they went. When she spoke, Alice kept her eyes straight ahead. “You could just not marry him,” Alice said quietly, almost indistinguishable over the noise of traffic. It wasn’t the first time Alice had said this to her, and it certainly wasn’t going to be the last.

The memory of Alice finding out about the marriage was still clear in her mind. Tipsy, indignant Alice grabbing Rio by the shoulders and spewing half-formed plans about running away and changing their identities. When Rio had laughed and shaken her off, telling her she didn’t want to leave or change her name or do any of that, Alice had said the same thing. Just don’t marry him. 

Now, Rio’s smile softened into something mournful. “We both know I can’t do that.”

Reluctantly, Alice met her gaze. She nodded once before looking away, lips pressed together. 

If there was anyone who would understand the pressure of doing right by her parents, after everything they sacrificed for her, it was Alice. It had been a long, tearful conversation the night Rio broke the news to her, but at the end of it, there had been a painful resignation. Alice didn't like it, but she understood it. After all, Alice’s mother had died for her to be where she was today, something Alice hated to talk about. It didn’t get any more guilt-inducing than that.

“You deserve to be happy,” was all Alice said.

Rio shrugged, “Yeah, well, who’s actually happy these days?”

Alice looked like she wanted to say something, but after a moment, she shook her head and asked how her plants were doing. It was easier to pretend everything was normal with a topic like that, and Rio relished in falling into the comfort of talking to Alice. It had always felt natural with Alice, like finding a kindred spirit. 

That feeling was what Rio clung to as they stepped inside the bridal boutique, immediately blinded by all different shades of white in every material imaginable. Rio sidled closer to Alice, standing half-behind her as if she might be able to protect her from what was to come. 

Rio’s thumb had just jammed itself into the cuticle of her index fingers when Paola called out, “Rio, over here!”

In the back corner of the boutique, Paola, Evanora, and Agatha were waiting for them. While Paola and Evanora sat together on one of the couches, Agatha sat in a single chair, arms crossed. Rio wondered if Agatha had come from work, given the tight pencil skirt and blouse she wore. It cut a much more feminine figure of her, but no less domineering. 

Rio forced her eyes away from her as she walked up to the group.

“Hello,” Rio greeted, giving a polite nod. “I hope you weren’t waiting too long.”

“Just a few minutes,” Paola said. She stood up and hugged her briefly, and to Rio’s relief, Evanora and Agatha made no move to do the same. “It gave us a chance to pick out some dresses for you already.”

“Yay,” Rio said, trying to sound excited, but going by both Alice and Agatha’s snorts, it wasn’t very convincing. Rio elbowed her friend and said, “This is Alice, everyone. My friend from college. She’ll be my maid of honor.” That was the deal. They would each have one person standing with them at the altar. For Rio, it would Alice. For James, it would be Agatha. 

“It’s nice to meet all of you,” Alice said with a perfunctory smile.

“Your English is very good,” Evanora replied, to which Alice looked at Rio with wide eyes.

When Rio could only wince, Alice said, “Thanks, I sure hope it is. I grew up here.”

This made Agatha smother a laugh, hand trying to hide her smile. It was a relief, if Rio had to be honest, to know that someone else recognized the absurdity of the comment, even if it was Agatha. Evanora only tilted her head though, considering her. “And where are you from?”

“I’m from California.”

Agatha didn’t quite hide her laugh that time, earning herself a glare from Evanora. “Your family,” Evanora said, a thread of disdain obvious in her voice. 

“Korea,” Alice said, and Rio could feel the way she’d grown tense beside her. This was getting too close to talking about her mother, and Rio knew Evanora wouldn’t let it go if they got onto that topic. “And before you ask, South Korea.”

“Okay,” Rio blurted out. She stepped forward, physically blocking Alice from Evanora’s view. “Dresses? You mentioned dresses. Where are they?”

“Yes, there are so many for you to try on,” Paola said, acting as if the previous exchange hadn’t happened at all. Paola’s smile hadn’t faltered once, even at Evanora’s more ignorant remarks. Rio wondered if Evanora had made the same comment when she first met Rio’s parents. Could Evanora even point to Puerto Rico on a map? “Let’s go to the dressing room,” Paola said, gently pushing Rio. 

Rio let herself be steered to the dressing room, but she couldn’t help but glance over her shoulder to check on Alice as she went. Her friend only smiled and shrugged before pointedly choosing to sit in the chair on the other side of Agatha. Rio wasn’t sure what to think of Agatha and Alice talking, but at least Agatha, while a bit of a jerk, wouldn’t be racist. Hopefully.

“What if I don’t find one?” Rio asked as they walked. It was a genuine concern she’d had, forgotten momentarily by Evanora’s comments. “What if I hate all of them?” No dress, no wedding, right? Rio almost laughed at herself. Yeah, right.

“You will find a dress,” Paola said firmly.

“How will I know?”

“You’ll just know.”

Rio rolled her eyes and stepped into the dressing room.

Knowing she’d be trying on all sorts of dresses, Rio had put on a strapless bra and nude underwear, and that was what she stripped down to once inside. There was a silk, white robe hanging off one of the hooks inside, and Rio shrugged it on while she waited for the first dress to arrive.

Unsurprisingly, it was extravagant with a skirt so poofy that Rio was sure she’d drown in it. With help from one of the boutique’s workers, a quiet but efficient woman named Tessa, Rio put it on. Rio looked at herself in the mirror before she walked out. She wrinkled her nose, and Tessa wore a sympathetic smile as she grabbed the train so Rio wouldn’t trip.

That was just the beginning. Dress after dress, Rio found herself in over-the-top gowns that she would never wear, not even on her wedding day. While the dresses picked out by Paola were borderline gaudy, the ones chosen by Evanora were even worse. They were modest, almost comically so. They all had high necklines and long sleeves, barely hugging Rio’s figure. Rio was beginning to think Evanora was picking out all the ugly ones on purpose.

“What’s the longest you’ve had people try on dresses?” Rio asked as Tessa helped her take off her twentieth dress.

“Do you really want to know?” Tessa replied. When Rio just stared, Tessa said, “Nine hours. From open to close.”

“Seriously?” Rio gaped. 

Tessa nodded, “Mother-in-law had a lot of opinions, and let’s just say the bride didn’t agree.” She gave Rio a conciliatory pat on the shoulder. “Hey, maybe if you’re lucky, they’ll let you stop for lunch.” With that, she slipped out to grab the next round of dresses.

Rio groaned and dug the heels of her hands into her eyes. This was ridiculous. She was either going to get married looking like a fairy tale princess or a failed nun, and both options sounded generally terrible. Rio might not care about this wedding, but that didn’t mean she wanted to look bad either. Knowing her parents, not to mention the Harknesses, photos of her were going to be in at least one or two magazines.

When she heard the curtain to the dressing room open, Rio dropped her hands and turned around, expecting her mother or Tessa. Instead, it was Agatha standing in the doorway, eyes slowly roving over her bare body. 

“Agatha!” Rio gasped. She ripped the robe off the hook and wrapped it around herself haphazardly. “What the hell are you doing?”

Agatha’s eyes finally snapped up to meet hers. Rio wasn’t sure if she was imagining how dark they looked. She blinked a few times, as if she was coming back to herself. Agatha looked down at her hand then lifted the hanger up. “My mother asked me to bring you another dress,” she said. 

“Well, you’ve brought it,” Rio said curtly. “Thanks.”

Agatha walked further into the dressing room. The hanger rested on a single finger. She tilted her head and asked, “You don’t need any help?”

“The worker can help me,” Rio said, fighting the urge to take a step back. 

“Are you sure? I don’t mind.” Agatha stopped right beside her and ran her hand down Rio’s spine. She splayed it against the small of her back, and Rio was reminded of James doing the same at dinner. Was that a thing with this family? A seemingly friendly yet possessive touch? Agatha's hand was smaller than James's but her long fingers dug in, warm through the thin fabric of the robe.

Rio stepped away now, folding her arms over her chest. “I’m sure,” she said. “Get out. Please.”

Agatha didn’t leave immediately. She kept looking at Rio with those blue eyes, haunting in their beauty. Her lips twitched into a smile, and for a second, she looked as though she might say something. Agatha said nothing though. She took one slow step back before she turned and left without another word. 

Rio let out a sigh of relief once she was gone. She hadn’t let herself dwell too long, or rather, at all, on her confusing feelings for Agatha, and after this, Rio was annoyed to find that she found her just as attractive and infuriating as last time.

When the curtain was drawn open again, Rio snapped, “God, didn’t I tell you to leave?”

It wasn’t Agatha standing there this time. It was Alice, arms full of something white, with a raised brow. “Someone’s cranky,” Alice remarked. She shut the curtain behind her and dropped into the lone chair in the dressing room. “I’d ask how you’re doing, but the answer is obvious.”

“I just want to be done,” Rio sighed.

“Who’s worse? Your mom, his mom, or his sister?” Alice asked. She wore that teasing half-smile, just like she always did when she was trying to cheer her up. “Personally, I think his mom has a special place reserved in hell.”

“What gave it away? The dresses that cover me up more than a nun’s habit or the casual racism?” Rio snorted.

“I was just talking about the dresses, but if you want to unpack the fact that you’ll be dealing with that for the rest of your life, be my guest.”

“No, let’s keep that sealed up tight,” Rio said quickly. If she thought too long about that, she’d lose her mind well before the wedding. She walked over to Alice and nudged the fabric in her lap. “Let’s talk about what you’ve got there.”

“A dress that’s actually something you’d wear,” Alice said with a proud smile. “You’re not the only one tired. I think Agatha might murder Evanora first honestly.”

“Now, I’d pay to see that,” Rio murmured. She took the dress from Alice and gave her a warm smile. “Thanks for doing this. Being here.”

Alice gently kicked her leg and said, “Are you kidding? I just love spending my Saturday making small talk with your future sister-in-law, who, by the way, isn’t nearly as bad as you made her seem.”

“So, she’s not a cocky asshole?” 

“No, she definitely is,” Alice said, and Rio laughed. Alice grinned and continued, “I don’t know though. She kind of owns it, you know? And at least with her, you know where you stand. After all these years, I still can’t tell if your mom likes me, and Evanora? I don’t think she likes me, but she looks at me like she’s wondering if I could do the math on her taxes for her.”

Rio chuckled and sent Alice out, so she could change. Knowing where you stand with Agatha? It didn’t sound quite right to her. Rio had no idea where she stood with Agatha. While she was fairly confident Agatha didn’t hate her, she didn’t have much more than that. Based on their last dinner and today, Agatha seemed to find her amusing, like a toy to entertain her during the wedding proceedings.

Maybe that was all she was to Agatha, and Rio actually did know where she stood with her.

When Tessa returned, Rio put on the dress Alice brought her. It was a simple dress with long sleeves that cuffed at the end, leaving them to billow slightly. The skirt fell loosely around her, no poof to be found, and the bodice was fitted. The neckline dipped lower than Rio would have chosen for herself, but it admittedly looked flattering on her.

“Your friend has good taste,” Tessa said. She clipped Rio’s hair into an updo and pinned a veil into the top of it to complete the look. For the first time all morning, Rio didn’t hate her reflection.  “Let’s see what everyone else thinks.”

As soon as she walked out, Rio watched everyone’s faces brighten at the sight of her in the dress, but the most surprising was Agatha.

Instead of the sneer she’d been wearing the last few hours, Agatha’s face had softened into something Rio wanted to call awe. She wasn’t sure what to call it because she’d never seen Agatha look at her like this before. Eyes wide, lips parted. Vulnerable in its honesty. Rio could see the exact moment Agatha realized she was staring because the expression was gone in an instant, smoothing out into the indifferent frown from before.

“This one,” Rio blurted out, eyes still on Agatha. “This is the one.”

“You look gorgeous! Like a real bride!” Paola cried. She leapt to her feet and swept Rio into a hug. Somewhere, to the side, Evanora was saying something about adding fabric to the neckline to make it more appropriate. “I told you that you would know,” Paola told her, kissing her cheek. “You always know.”

Rio smiled, but it was less genuine than before. She had known, just like she said, but it wasn’t for any reason Rio would have guessed. It wasn’t seeing herself in the mirror. It wasn’t watching her mother’s overjoyed reaction. It wasn’t Alice trying to act tough even as her eyes teared up. It wasn’t even the dizzying realization that the wedding was really happening that made Rio know that this was the dress for her. 

It was Agatha looking at her like she was beautiful.

Why the hell had she looked at her like that in the first place?

Rio was wrong. She had no idea where she stood with Agatha at all, and suddenly, she wasn’t so sure if Agatha knew either.

Chapter 3

Chapter Summary

After an awkward coffee date, Rio finds herself alone with Agatha for the cake tasting.

Rio stared at her half-drunk coffee as her fingers tapped absently against the side of the mug.

Across from her, James looked like he was just as lost and uncomfortable as her.

For the last half hour, the two of them sat in a coffee shop, trading stilted small talk. There was only so much to say to someone about how your work and family was though. Even the wedding talk had run dry. If she cared enough, Rio knew she could have shared a funny story from work or talked about her plants, but she didn’t care. She didn’t want to be here. The only reason she was here was because her mother tricked her into thinking she was meeting her for coffee, not James.

It had been almost a week since Rio bought her wedding dress, and the purchase only seemed to worsen her malaise. The reality of her situation was settling into the recesses of her mind slowly but surely, and with every day that they drew closer to the wedding, Rio felt her anxiety climb. 

“Listen,” James finally said. He sat back in his chair, running a hand through his hair before he smoothed it out in a compulsive move. “I understand this wasn’t your choice. It wasn’t really mine either, to be honest, but it doesn’t have to be bad. Or weird.” James flashed a smile that was almost boyish. Maybe if Rio liked men, she would have found it attractive. As it was, Rio just tried not to sigh.

“I agree,” Rio said. “I just want us to be…” She trailed off. She actually wasn’t sure what she wanted them to be. “Friends?” It came out as a question. It seemed like the easiest answer. Better than strangers, certainly better than enemies or lovers.

“What, you don’t think you’ll fall for my charms eventually?” James joked.

Rio forced a laugh and simply said, “No, I don’t think so.”

Thankfully, James didn’t look offended. He shrugged, saying, “Okay. Friends then.” He glanced at his watch and said, “Maybe we’ll have a proper conversation next time. For now though, I have to get to a meeting.”

“Have fun,” Rio offered. It seemed like the polite thing to do, even if it came out a bit more sarcastic than she meant. 

James just smirked though. He said, “It’s about taxes. I’ll be lucky if I don’t fall asleep.” He stood up and hesitated for a moment. Rio tensed, hoping he wouldn’t try to touch her. James smiled awkwardly and said, “Have fun at the cake tasting. It sounds like you’ll be having more fun than me.” He gave her a brief wave before he departed, leaving a twenty dollar bill on the table as he did.

Rio didn’t even try to hide her envy as she watched him leave. Of course, James didn’t have to be involved in the wedding planning. He didn’t have to sit through endless appointments and attend to little details he didn’t care about. Rio did though. Rio had to clear her schedule and spend day after day with their mothers, organizing a wedding that really just needed her to show up for. More than once, Rio considered asking for just the time and place and saying, “See you there.”

Paola would never let that happen, and neither would Evanora. The fallout of even trying that would be unimaginable. No, Rio was trapped in this nuptial hellscape. One that would be continuing well into the afternoon as she went to try various cake flavors. At least with this errand, Rio was being fed.

Rio killed another half hour at the coffee shop, scrolling on her phone and sipping at her now cold coffee, before she caught a cab to the bakery. During the ride, she got a text from Paola, informing her that she wasn’t going to make it. Rio rolled her eyes. She wished she could start charging these people for her time, especially if they weren’t going to be involved themselves.

When Rio arrived at the bakery, she was surprised to find only Agatha standing out front. She got out of the cab slowly, approaching her the same way you would a predator in the wild. Although, that was more or less what Agatha actually was. Today, she wore black slacks that hugged her ass and a striped button-up. A simple look but it still looked so much nicer than the jeans and t-shirt Rio had thrown on. 

“Hey,” Rio greeted her. “Where’s your mom?”

“Busy,” Agatha said. “Where’s yours?”

Rio felt like she’d be knocked upside the head very hard with something very heavy. That was the only way to explain the way she suddenly felt so dizzy. “Busy,” Rio repeated back. She blinked a few times, trying to wake herself from this nightmare scenario.

“Oh, would you relax?” Agatha rolled her eyes. “You look like you’re about to throw up.” She crossed her arms over her chest and said, “I don’t bite.”

“Are you sure about that?” Rio asked warily. Agatha definitely looked like she would bite, whether as an attack or as foreplay, Rio wasn’t sure.

Agatha batted her eyelashes at her and said, “Wouldn’t you like to know?”

Rio shook her head, hoping her blush wasn’t too obvious. “Whatever,” Rio muttered. “Let’s just get this over with.”

Once the names Vidal and Harkness were mentioned inside the bakery, the two of them were earnestly ushered into a separate room where the owner promised to bring out a slice of every possible combination for them. Rio half-heartedly told him that wasn’t necessary, already expecting the vehement insistence that they try everything they had to offer.

“Someone’s looking for a good tip,” Agatha muttered.

“More like they’re hoping we tell every other rich person we know to come here,” Rio sighed. 

It had been over twenty years since Rio’s family began their ascent from scrounging to make ends meet to high profile political assets, but Rio had never fully accepted or adjusted to the change. As stupid as it was, especially given how privileged she was now, Rio longed for the days where Luis and she would sit on the stoop of their apartment building and share a bar of chocolate as a secret treat just between the two of them. Things had been simpler then.

As slices of cakes were brought out in a seemingly endless rotation, Rio took an obligatory bite of each one, making note of which ones she liked on the paper they gave her. Agatha did the same, but with every bite she took, she had a comment along to go with it.

“This tastes like a child was set loose in the kitchen,” Agatha said after trying a vanilla cake filled with colorful sprinkles and covered in a sickeningly sweet icing. A moment later, she said, pointing to another slice, “This one tastes like someone’s grandmother’s perfume got dropped into the batter.”

If Rio didn’t know any better, she would have thought Agatha was trying to cheer her up. As it was, she probably liked the sound of her own voice so much that she couldn’t resist filling the silence with it.

Rio merely hummed and nodded to whatever Agatha said, but apparently, that wasn’t enough attention for her because Agatha finally said, “Is my brother that awful that wedding planning makes you look like you’d rather put a gun to your head?”

“What?” Rio said, startled. She processed what Agatha said and shook her head hastily. “No. He’s fine. I just…” She winced. “Don’t care.”

Once again, Rio saw a strange resemblance between the two siblings as Agatha didn’t seem offended at all, shrugging. When James shrugged though, it was kind of jerky, like he wasn’t in complete control of his limbs. When Agatha shrugged, it was an oddly graceful movement, like she couldn’t have cared less. Rio watched as Agatha pressed her fork against one of the cake slices, making it crumble. Without looking at her, Agatha asked, “Didn’t dream about white dresses and flowers as a little girl?”

“No, I’m pretty sure I was too busy trying to catch squirrels,” Rio said honestly.

She tried to hide her smile at the way Agatha’s head perked up, a startled expression on her face. Agatha dropped her fork and looked at her properly. “Squirrels?” Agatha repeated before she shook her head and asked, “Why were you trying to catch them?”

“I wanted one for a pet,” Rio explained. “My apartment wouldn’t let us have dogs or cats, but I figured a squirrel was small enough to hide.” She bit her lip and added, before she could stop herself, “I also heard from an older kid in the complex that they dissected a squirrel at school, and I thought I could do the same if I caught one.”

“You’re weird,” Agatha said with an odd sense of admiration. There wasn’t a trace of disgust or judgement.

Rio ducked her head, feeling her cheeks redden. She’d said that to throw Agatha off, to bring back some of the scorn she was used to seeing from her. Instead, she felt like she’d left herself open to her eyes, sharp and knowing. Rio cleared her throat and looked back up, asking, “What about you? Did you ever dream about having a wedding?”

“Me?” Agatha snorted. “No.” She didn’t elaborate, and Rio didn’t press.

After that though, it became easier to talk to Agatha. They mainly spoke about wedding planning, and it exposed the biggest difference Rio found between the Harkness siblings so far. 

James was undeniably easy-going with his charm being how he seemed to simply accept things and move on, even if he disagreed. Rio noticed it when they had coffee earlier. When Rio told him about what they’d decided on the wedding so far, she’d catch him making a face. It prompted Rio to ask if he wanted her to change anything, but he had just smiled and assured her that whatever she chose would be fine.

Meanwhile, Agatha, who wasn’t even the one getting married, had something to say about everything, it seemed. Rio couldn’t simply tell Agatha that the wedding colors were navy blue and gold. She had to tell the insufferable woman why the wedding colors were navy blue and gold, only for Agatha to tell her why she would never want that for her wedding. It went on like that for everything.

It was exasperating, being more or less lectured about why her wedding was going to be awful, but it was also refreshing to speak to someone who somehow abhorred the whole thing even more than her. Agatha was one of the only people to tell her that this whole thing was stupid, even if she was coming from a place of aesthetics, and Rio admittedly enjoyed hearing that more than she should. 

Agatha was growing on her in a weird way because of this. Or maybe Rio was just that desperate to find some kind of camaraderie. 

“Was there anyone else in the picture when your parents asked you to marry my brother?” Agatha asked as they sampled their last round of cakes.

Asked was a much kinder way of phrasing how her parents had guilted her into this whole thing, but Rio still answered, “No. I haven’t dated in a while.”

Rio hadn’t dated anyone seriously since college, and even then, Rio had been secretive, nervous, and terrified. Dating her during that time consisted of a lot of dates in her apartment, and while her girlfriend at the time had understood, it had also ultimately been the reason they broke up.

Since then, Rio occasionally hooked up with women, but it was never more than once. It wasn’t what Rio wanted at all since she’d always been a bit of a romantic, but that wasn’t exactly possible then. It certainly wasn’t possible now.

Before her mood could be completely ruined, Rio said, “Should I even bother asking you if there’s anyone in the picture?”

“Depends on what you mean by in the picture,” Agatha replied with a shameless grin. “But there’s always someone.”

“Classy,” Rio snorted.

“Well, of course,” Agatha said with exaggerated condescension. “I’m a Harkness, dear.”

The two of them shared a smile just as one of the workers came in to clean up the plates. It was an older woman, probably in her sixties or seventies. She smiled warmly at them and said, “I hope you enjoyed everything. When’s the wedding?”

“Thank you, we did,” Rio said. “It’ll be June 5th.” 

The woman's eyes went wide as she said, “Well, isn’t that soon!” Then, she blushed and said, “I apologize. I meant to say congratulations.” She looked between them and added, “The two of you make a beautiful couple.”

Rio’s mouth fell open while Agatha sat up, waving her hands.

“Couple?” Agatha repeated. “No, no, no. Not us.” Rio half-listened as Agatha explained the situation, distracted by the way her pale skin turned bright red, spreading across her cheeks and all the way down her neck until it disappeared beneath her shirt. It was the first time Rio had ever seen her flustered. It was endearing, seeing the usually overly confident woman fumble with her words.

After the woman left, Agatha refused to look at her. Her face was still flushed, and she fidgeted with the rings on her hands. 

Rio decided to have mercy on her. “Thanks for staying,” she said. When Agatha turned to her in confusion, Rio explained, “You didn’t have to stay with me, especially when neither of our mothers were here to make you.”

Agatha didn’t say anything, turning to look out the window. Her fingers still messed with one of her rings, spinning it around and around. “It was nothing,” Agatha said. “Just eating some cake.” When Rio opened her mouth to argue, Agatha added, so quietly under her breath Rio wondered if she was meant to hear it at all, “Someone should be with you for this.”

Rio didn’t know what to say to that, so she cleared her throat and picked up her paper. “So, I was thinking about choosing the chocolate.”

Chapter 4

Chapter Summary

Just as the wedding stress gets to her, Rio is invited out for drinks by Agatha.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio was one week away from her wedding and one conversation with her mother away from completely losing her mind. 

Even though it seemed as though everything was planned, Paola kept finding more, inconsequential things to fuss over. She couldn’t just deal with it herself though. No, Paola just had to show up at her apartment at all hours of the day to pester her about it, as if Rio wasn’t going to just tell her to do whatever she wanted anyways.

The latest issue was the type of lighting for the venue. There were three different settings, along with a truly egregious number of options for additional lighting. Rio hadn’t done the math, but she was pretty sure there were more than fifty variations. As Paola went through each of them, they began to blur together too, making it feel like there were closer to ten that she just kept going over.

“What do you think?” Paola asked.

“Whatever you want,” Rio said tiredly. 

Paola sighed, like Rio was the difficult one here, and said, “Rio, this will determine how you look in your photos. Let’s really think about it.”

Rio was saved from responding when her phone lit up in a call. She eagerly snatched it up, only to pause when she saw it was Agatha who was calling her. Although they’d exchanged numbers at their mothers’ insistence, just in case, they had never bothered to text or call each other. 

Since the cake tasting, Rio had seen Agatha twice, once to finalize the seating arrangement and again to choose Agatha’s bridesmaid dress. Both times had only worsened Rio’s growing feelings for the other woman.

While they planned the seating chart, Rio could see Evanora regret inviting her daughter every time Agatha made a snide suggestion. The highlight was actually when Agatha said it was imperative to sit a divorced couple together to remind them of where they failed. Apparently, Agatha informed her in a whisper, the husband had cheated with his business partner’s wife, who he would also be bringing to the wedding. Agatha wanted to run a bet on who would snap first. Her best guess was the ex-wife. Rio agreed. Evanora and Paola had ignored them both.

For Agatha’s bridesmaid dress, Rio had actually tried to get out of going. Like everything else about the wedding, Rio didn’t care. Agatha could have shown up in a neon yellow dress, or hell, even white, and Rio would have been fine with it. 

Paola insisted though, so Rio had shown up in sweat pants and a cap in protest. It’d gotten her a stern look from Paola and a reproachful look from Evanora, but it had been worth being able to comfortably sink into one of the chairs and sulk. Not to mention, Agatha had looked like she wished she was wearing that instead of the parade of dresses Evanora had picked out for her.

In the end, Agatha ended up with a satin dress in a color reminiscent of the night sky. It was a halter neck and floor length, but it left most of her back bare. Evanora had tried to protest it, but Paola had gushed over the dress and how Agatha looked in it, singing it praises, until Evanora had reluctantly agreed. To Rio’s amusement, Evanora had also made sure to buy her a wrap to go with it.

When they asked Rio for her opinion, she had tried to focus her eyes on everything but the bare skin revealed by the dress. She ended up looking somewhere over Agatha's head as she said, “It’s nice. You should get it.” From the edge of her periphery, Rio had seen Agatha smile.

As she picked up the call, Rio couldn’t quite hide her confusion as she said, “Hello?”

“Rio,” Agatha said, sounding surprised that she answered. “Good. Hello. How does a drink sound?”

“Amazing,” Rio said without hesitation.

“Okay, then repeat after me: Yes, Agatha. I can meet you right now. I know that’s important to your mother.” 

Rio’s mouth opened, but she hesitated. Was she really going to just trust Agatha and meet her for a drink? Although they seemed to have reached a commonground, Rio wouldn’t exactly say they were close enough to just hang out with each other. It was an excuse to get away from her mother though, not to mention see Agatha, so Rio said, “Yeah, Agatha. I can meet you. I know that’s important to your mother.” 

“Good girl,” Agatha said, and Rio’s hand tightened around her phone. “I’ll meet you at Salem in half an hour.” Then, without another word or explanation, Agatha hung up.

“Is everything okay?” Paola asked.

Rio stared at her phone dumbly for a moment before she nodded slowly. “Yeah, Agatha just needs me to come over and help out with something for Evanora. I think something about the guest list,” Rio lied.

“I won’t keep you then,” Paola said. She stood up from her couch and cupped Rio’s cheek. It was a tender touch, and Rio found herself caught between tensing and leaning into it. “I’m glad you’re getting along with Agatha. She’ll be your family soon.”

“I have a family,” Rio said with a roll of her eyes.

“Your family is growing,” Paola replied. “It’s a good thing, Rio.”

Rio clamped her mouth shut and walked her mother to the door. Once she was gone, Rio went to her bedroom to change. Something told her that track pants and a t-shirt wouldn’t work for wherever she was meeting Agatha. She dug through her closet, holding up various shirts and pants, before she settled on a pair of dark jeans and a black shirt with the top buttons undone. 

The bar Agatha told her to meet her at ended up being a lot more casual than Rio expected. It was the kind of place where people went to grab a drink with coworkers after work, and that looked to be the majority of the people there as Rio walked inside. Looking around, Rio took in the simple, vintage aesthetic and low lighting that made the bar feel intimate.

Rio was debating whether to go to the bar when she felt a hand on her back. She tensed at first before she registered the familiar press of long fingers. Rio swallowed before she turned and found Agatha at her side, dressed in a fitted, black dress. She looked like she just came from work.  

“Glad you could make it,” Agatha said. “I reserved a table.”

“You were that confident I would come?” Rio asked as she followed her. 

Agatha smiled and replied, “I would have used the table either way.”

Rio wasn’t sure that was true, but she didn’t call her on it. The table was a circular booth tucked away, half-hidden behind some plants. It was private. Rio was both relieved yet nervous at the fact, and she tried not to think too hard about it as she offered to grab them their drinks.

Unsurprisingly, Agatha wanted a martini, and Rio rolled her eyes when Agatha informed her, “I like it extra dirty.” 

Once they had their drinks, Rio wasted no time, saying, “So, how’d you know?” Agatha raised a brow, and Rio clarified, “That I’d need this.”

“My mother was starting to stress me out,” Agatha explained. Her index finger tapped idly against the table. “If that was what was happening with me, I could only imagine what your mother must have been doing to you.” 

“And why help me?” Rio asked. 

Agatha looked amused, a smirk on her lips. “I’m not so heartless as to let you go insane,” she said, only to follow it up with, “There’s plenty of time for that after you’re married to my brother.” Rio’s laugh was quiet, barely a huff, but Agatha looked immensely pleased to have gotten the reaction. “See? Aren’t I so kind? You’re relaxed already.”

“Don’t flatter yourself,” Rio replied. She took a pointed sip of her rum and coke. “It’s the alcohol.”

“Oh, is that it?” Agatha hummed.

Her first drink went quickly as Rio complained about the last week, lamenting her mother’s obsession about every detail. It was easy to talk to Agatha, and maybe Rio shouldn't be surprised by that anymore, but she was. There was something about the way Agatha seemed so focused on her when she spoke, the clever retort she had to every story. It was the kind of chemistry Rio didn't find often.

By the time she was starting her third drink, Rio felt warm and lazy. Her head lolled against the back of the booth as she stared at Agatha, whose cheeks were flushed and eyes were hazy.

Agatha toyed with the toothpick her olive had come on and said, “Don’t you think about just saying fuck it and skipping town?” 

Rio didn’t answer at first. She was certainly feeling the effects of her drinks, but she wasn’t so far gone as to not recognize the danger in answering this honestly. Instead, Rio turned it on her, asking, “Is that what you would do?” 

“Honey, I wouldn’t have gotten engaged in the first place,” Agatha said with a harsh laugh. “In case you’ve forgotten, I’m not exactly one to do as my mother says.” She wrinkled her nose, and Rio smiled at how cute it was, the way her nose crinkled and lips twisted. “You didn’t answer my question, you know.”

“That was on purpose,” Rio said. She thought she’d let it go, but then Agatha tilted her head and fucking pouted at her. It shouldn’t have worked, this grown, infuriating woman pouting at her, but it did. Apparently, Agatha could be stupidly adorable when she wanted to be. Or maybe, she was just this cute because they were both drunk. Rio sighed and said, “My parents, they gave up a lot for me. They worked so hard for me to have this life, and what kind of daughter would that make me if I just spat in their face and ran away?”

Agatha sounded like she couldn’t decide whether she was angry or confused. “So that’s it? They just get to have your life when they already have their own?” 

“You don’t understand,” Rio said.

“Then make me understand.” 

Rio turned her head and found Agatha much closer than she expected. When had she moved? They started the night a few feet away, but now, Agatha was less than a foot from her. Rio blinked hard as she tried to remember her words. This close up, Rio couldn’t help but notice the pink of Agatha’s lips and the long, dark lashes that framed her blue eyes. 

“I don’t think you can,” Rio said, speaking so softly that Agatha leaned in even closer to hear her. Rio didn’t move away. Instead, she tilted her head forward. “My family couldn’t afford for me to have a rebellious phase. We weren’t destitute or anything, but we scrimped a lot when I was a kid. Nothing extravagant, nothing fancy. A lot of box dinners and stuff.” Rio licked her lips, trying to find the words. “If I had even a fraction of the scandals you had when you were younger, it would have been over for us. We didn’t have the money or status to sweep things under the rug and keep our standing. All we had was my father working his ass off, charming the right people and letting other men treat him like a dog to let him in on their connections.” Rio’s lips curled into a humorless smile. “Do you know what that’s like?” 

“Rio–”

“My parents fought for their place here,” Rio told her. “And I’m not going to let my selfishness ruin that.”

Agatha didn’t say anything for a moment. She just let her eyes, so impossibly blue, bore into hers. Finally, Agatha came even closer and whispered, “And is that what you think of me? Some spoiled, selfish brat who’s never struggled a day in her life?”

No, that wasn’t what Rio thought at all, but to hear Agatha take what she said and boil it down to something like that, Rio couldn’t help but say, “Yes, that’s exactly what I think.”

Rio thought she saw a flash of hurt cross Agatha’s face, but it was gone before she was sure. She thought about apologizing, but then Agatha leaned in, not to say anything but close enough that their lips almost touched. Rio stopped breathing. She jerked away, not far enough to create any real distance between them but just enough to keep her head from spinning. Just a scant few inches that made it possible for Rio to breathe again.

“You’re right, Rio,” Agatha murmured. Her eyes were half-lidded, but Rio could see the way her pupils had almost swallowed her irises. “I am selfish.” Her hand, hidden beneath the table, reached out and grabbed a fistful of Rio’s shirt. Rio gasped, but still, she didn’t move. Agatha leaned in, letting their noses brush. Rio could feel her breath hot against her lips. “Tell me to stop.” 

Agatha’s hand was tight around her shirt, curling slowly so that Rio was drawn closer ever so slowly. Agatha tilted her head closer, but then she moved away, her lips ghosting just out of reach. Both of their breathing was heavy and uneven, and Rio wondered if this was what it was like before they’d even kissed, what would happen after?

Agatha licked her lips. Her eyes fluttered shut, and she leaned in with purpose.

Rio’s eyes slammed shut.

“Stop.”

Her breath was trembling when she opened her eyes again. Agatha stared at her with an unreadable expression for so long that a part of Rio recklessly thought about kissing her anyways. Just as the traitorous thought crossed her mind, Agatha let go of her shirt and pulled away completely, moving to sit at a respectable distance.

Her eyes were glassy, staring off into space. Her hands clenched around the stem of her martini glass. “You should go,” Agatha said. “I’ll cover the bill.”

“Agatha–”

“Rio.”

Their eyes met, and Rio fell silent. She wanted to say something, but she didn’t know what.

“Good night, Rio,” Agatha said with a note of finality.

Rio shut her eyes for a moment and sighed. When she opened them again, she said, “Good night, Agatha.”

Getting up from the booth felt impossible. Her head was spinning, and her legs felt weak; both had nothing to do with what she’d drunk tonight.

Although she didn’t look back, Rio could feel Agatha’s eyes on her as she left. 

Stepping into the warm summer air, Rio buried her face in her hands and tried to ignore the tears that pricked at the corners of her eyes and the panic that clawed its way up her throat.

Rio couldn’t do this. She could not do this. She could not have feelings for her future sister-in-law. This had to just be some stupid crush, something she’d get over eventually. Right?

A muffled sob tore at her throat.

By the time a cab arrived, her eyes were swollen and her throat was scratchy. Hazily, dangerously, Rio wondered what would happen if she turned around and went back into the bar. 

Rio got into the cab, and she went home.

Chapter End Notes

their tension is beginning to consume my every thought

Chapter 5

Chapter Summary

Despite her protests, Rio has a bachelorette party, and naturally, as her future sister-in-law, Agatha is invited.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The party had just begun, and Rio was already pleasantly buzzed.

It was the night before her wedding, and at Alice’s insistence, Rio was having a bachelorette party. With some generous funding from her parents, Alice had rented out the penthouse suite of a hotel downtown and invited Natasha, Maria, and Gamora, their friends from college, to drink and eat to their hearts’ content. As far as bachelorette parties went, Rio knew this was a fairly subdued one, but even this felt like too much. 

“Come on,” Natasha said, plopping down beside her on the couch. She shoved another shot into her hand. “Enjoy yourself. Who knows when the next time you’ll be able to do this will be.”

“I’m getting married,” Rio replied. “Isn’t the idea that the next time is never?”

“Never say never,” Natasha smirked, guiding the shot up to Rio’s lips. Rio rolled her eyes but took the shot. “Attagirl. Now, remind me again why you’re getting married.” When Rio glared at her, Natasha waved her hand, “No, I mean, why this guy? There must be plenty of other boring men your parents could have pawned you off on.”

“Natasha,” Maria said warningly. 

“It’s a valid question,” Gamora said with a shrug.

The three of them turned to Rio expectantly while Alice sighed and announced she was opening another bottle of vodka. 

“He’s a Harkness,” Rio said, which should have been enough.

Natasha made a face though and said, “Explain it to me like I’m dumb. I don’t give a fuck about politics or business.” 

Gamora snorted while Maria rolled her eyes. Rio gratefully took the drink Alice gave her and took a large gulp. “They’re rich and well-connected,” Rio explained. “His family has been involved in politics probably since the U.S. was founded, whether it’s being actual politicians or providing money for campaigns. Not to mention, they’ve got stocks and shares in every major corporation that runs this country.” 

“Old money,” Gamora hummed. “So they’re conservative?” At Rio’s nod, Gamora raised a brow and said, “And he’s getting married to you?”

Once she slumped against the toilet, dizzy and seemingly done, she was helped to the nearest bed. Climbing into the bed, Rio noticed Venus was gone. So was Agatha.

Rio didn’t make it to the toilet before she threw up again.

Chapter 6

Chapter Summary

The wedding.

Chapter Notes

this one took a little longer, but between work and wanting to get this right, it was a bit of a struggle

i'm not sure i'm entirely satisfied, but i hope you enjoy this mess

Of all the different iterations Rio imagined her wedding day, not one of them included the mother of all hangovers making it impossible for her to see straight.

Rio was practically drowning herself in water in an attempt to feel less dehydrated. That, some pain medication, and a slice of toast was all that was holding her together at the moment.

Rio could not have told you much about getting ready for her wedding. She was vaguely aware of the flurry of movement around her, her mother at her side, scolding her for drinking too much, and the people doing her hair and make-up. It was around eleven in the morning, she was pretty sure, and the ceremony would be at two in the afternoon.

“How are you holding up?” Alice asked. She was the only one left from their friend group. Everyone else had been ushered out when Paola arrived that morning, and Rio was grateful to still have her here. She felt like the only piece of normalcy left.

“I feel like hell,” Rio muttered.

“I bet,” Alice laughed. “But they did a pretty good job at hiding that fact.”

Rio, who’d had her eyes closed the last hour to get her make-up done, looked at Alice through half-lidded eyes. “Yeah?” 

“See for yourself.”

When Rio opened her eyes fully, she could only stare. She’d never been particularly skilled with make-up, and most days, her hair was just down in its natural waves or up in a clip. It was jarring to see herself now, professional make-up making her skin look smooth and an elaborate bun at the base of her neck. It felt like looking at a stranger, and Rio couldn’t help but think that it seemed fitting for her to feel that way today. 

“You look beautiful,” Paola said, walking up to her side. She tenderly ran a hand over Rio’s hair and leaned down to press a kiss to her forehead. “Now, time to go. We’ll get you dressed at the church.”

In what felt like the blink of an eye, Rio was taken to the church where the ceremony was taking place, a beautiful church in Upstate New York, not far from the Harkness estate. It was an elegant, stone building with stained glass and ornate wood structures that felt a little bit like a fairy tale. If Rio had to give Catholicism anything, it was that the aesthetics were unmatched in their beauty.

“This is insane,” Rio mumbled under her breath as Alice helped her into her dress. It was just the two of them in the bridal suite. Her mother was off somewhere, yelling about flowers. It was a welcomed reprieve for Rio, a chance to breathe a little. “Alice, what am I doing?”

Alice’s hands paused over the buttons. She looked up and met Rio’s gaze in the mirror. “You’re getting married,” Alice said gently. She rested her hands on her shoulders and squeezed them. Her smile was a small quirk of her lips. “But if you’ve changed your mind, I’ll hotwire a car, and we can be out of here before your mom even notices we’re gone.”

Rio chuckled and felt tears prick the corners of her eyes. She wanted to say yes so badly. She wanted to rip off this dress and wipe off all of this make-up, and she wanted to run away and never look back. Rio was afraid though. To get married, yes, but also to disappoint her parents, to sow discord between them and ruin their relationship irreparably. She wanted her life, but was it worth the cost of losing her family?

A trembling breath left Rio before she whispered, “Just promise you’ll still be my friend?”

“Oh, Rio,” Alice sighed. She wrapped her arms around her waist and rested her head on her shoulder, hugging her tight. “You can’t get rid of me that easily, no matter how much your mother probably wishes that was true.”

Rio laughed and accepted the tissue Alice handed her. She dabbed at her eyes, trying her best not to ruin the make-up. She let Alice finish helping her into her dress and put on the veil. “For what it’s worth,” Alice said. “You make a beautiful bride.”

“Thanks,” Rio said softly. 

The two of them shared one more hug before Alice left to get ready herself, and Rio found herself alone for the first time all day. It was an odd feeling, the stillness and quietness that pervaded the room, but Rio savored it. It was likely her only chance for the rest of the day.

Standing in front of the mirror, Rio smoothed her hands over the skirt of the dress and took a deep breath. Instinctively, her hands came together, and her nails bit into the skin.

When Rio was a little girl, it was true that she didn’t dream about her wedding day. When she wasn’t chasing squirrels or climbing trees, Rio thought about wild adventures she’d go on. She would be an astronaut and see the stars. She would be a veterinarian and treat the most exotic of animals. She would be a pilot and travel the world. Rio had dreamed of a lot of things, and in every single one, she always imagined coming home to her parents to tell them about what she'd done.

Although both of her parents had been busy when Rio was growing up, she’d always felt their love. She felt it in the way Paola would always cook Rio’s favorite foods, especially if she knew she’d had a rough day. She felt it in the way Luis would sit and read with her every chance he had, using silly voices for the characters. Rio had always felt the value in her family, in her parents, but as she stood here on her wedding day, the weight of their love suddenly felt like a burden. His eyes grew misty at the sight of her, and there was nothing but adoration in his face. “My little girl,” Luis said. He didn’t hesitate to pull her into a hug, and Rio hugged him back, probably too tight but she didn’t care. “You are a sight to behold,” he murmured. He pulled back and ran his thumb over her cheek. “Are you ready?”

No.

Rio smiled, and Luis smiled back. The heaviness on her shoulders ebbed ever so slightly. “Yes,” Rio said. She took her father’s hand. “I am.”

Everyone else was gone by the time Rio stepped into the hall, and it was only a moment before it was her turn to go with her hand tucked into the crook of her father’s arm.

As she walked down the aisle, Rio felt herself begin to distance her mind from what was happening. It felt more like letting someone else walk down the aisle. That way, some small part of her whispered, it was like someone else was getting married too. Chapter Summary
