Second only to, perhaps, being married to Agatha's brother.

After she ignored the first text, Agatha texted her once more before she stopped. Her last text message taunted Rio every time she opened her phone. It was a simple, pointless text, but it was one that Rio couldn’t get out of her head.

Are you okay?

Without Agatha to fill her time, the days felt longer and the weeks dragged on. Those two months with Agatha felt like a dream in comparison to the bitter reality she’d forced herself into now. There were no more kisses that made her head spin or touches that made her breathless. There were no more teasing remarks or quiet confessions. 

A part of Rio was locked away now without Agatha to let her out.

Rio didn’t realize how much being with and without Agatha changed her until Alice told her one afternoon. The two of them were walking in the park, eating ice cream and enjoying some of the milder weather. Rio knew she wasn’t fully present with Alice, but she was trying her best to listen intently to whatever her best friend was telling her. 

Eventually though, Alice looked at her and said, “Are you okay?”

“Yeah,” Rio said immediately, even as she grimaced at the question. All it did was remind her of Agatha. When she received an unimpressed stare in response though, she sighed and said, “I don’t know.”

“Is everything okay with James?” Alice asked.

“Everything is great with James,” Rio answered honestly. 

Over the last two weeks, Rio and James spent more time together in the evenings, getting to know each other. They were now comfortable enough with each other that Rio began to see James more as a friend, rather than the man she was shackled to for the rest of her life. 

“Okay, so if it’s not James, is it the hospital?” Alice asked. When Rio shook her head, Alice sighed, “Then what is it, Rio? You’re being all weird and spacey today, like you’re on another planet. Not to mention, you’ve been kind of a bitch lately too.”

Rio didn’t say anything immediately. She wanted to tell Alice everything about her and Agatha, but she wasn’t sure how her best friend would react. Alice might have been willing to drive the getaway car on her wedding day, but that didn’t necessarily mean she’d condone cheating. 

Settling for a half-truth, Rio said, “I was hanging out with Agatha for a while.”

“The sister-in-law,” Alice said, to which Rio winced.

“Yeah,” Rio said, “and it was fun, having someone to talk to about all of this.” She saw Alice open her mouth and she hurried to say, “I know I can talk to you, but it’s different with her. She grew up in the same circles as me, and she knows James and Evanora.” Rio sighed and ran a hand through her hair. “But… I just don’t know if it’s such a good idea, being friends with Agatha.”

“Why not?” Alice said. She finished her ice cream and tossed it into a nearby trash can. She tilted her head thoughtfully and said, “I mean, even I’ve heard about her reputation at this point, but I don’t think that’s any reason not to be friends with her. You’re already married into her family anyways. There’s no distancing yourself from that.” 

Rio hummed in acknowledgement but let the conversation drop. Alice was right. There was no escaping Agatha, but the least Rio could do was try to have an appropriate relationship with her. One that wouldn’t blow up in her face, ruin her marriage, and taint her family’s reputation for the rest of her life. That was what Alice was encouraging anyways, wasn’t she? A friendship.

The thought almost made her laugh. She couldn’t imagine Agatha so easily agreeing to a measly friendship after two months of… Rio wasn’t even sure what to call it. She still hated the word affair. 

When it was time for them to go, Alice pulled Rio into a tight hug. Then, she cupped her face and looked Rio right in the eye, saying, “Take care of yourself, okay? Whatever the hell is wrong with you, don’t let it take over your life. You’re better than that, Rio.”

You’re better than that. Was she?

Rio nodded and hugged Alice again, fighting back the urge to cry and confess everything to her best friend. 

When she got back to the apartment, she waved to James and went to check on her plants on the terrace. It was a recent development, but James didn’t mind. He even encouraged her to buy more plants, even if he seemed a little baffled by her enjoyment of them. It was as Rio was watering a few of her plants that James poked his head out and said, “Don’t forget we have family dinner tonight.”

Rio nearly broke her neck with how quickly she looked up. “Already?”

“I know, right?” James laughed. “Feels like we just had one.”

There had been two family dinners since the night Rio fucked Agatha in her childhood bedroom. Unlike that one, the other two were nothing noteworthy. Dinner and drinks, and that was it. Rio and Agatha were perfectly civil around each other. That was how it had to be, if they didn’t want anyone to notice the fact that there was anything else going on. However, this would be the first dinner since Rio started avoiding Agatha. 

Needless to say, Rio wasn’t looking forward to it.

Still, she got dressed and got into the town car, letting James hold her hand during the drive out to the estate. During the car ride, Rio felt herself grow restless and suddenly remembered going to the estate with her parents all those months ago. The same urge to bolt filled her, just as it had then. In both cases, Rio stayed where she was.

When they arrived, James let out a quiet noise of surprise and said, “Agatha is here already.” He pointed out her town car. 

After hearing that, Rio stayed in the car for so long that James had to tap the window to break her from her reverie.  Shaking her head, Rio got out of the car and gave James a reassuring smile. She followed him into the house, but she kept herself just out of reach, so he wouldn’t take her hand again. 

Even though Rio knew that Agatha was here already, she still felt herself freeze, if only for the briefest moments, when she saw her. 

For the last few weeks, Rio had done everything she could to keep Agatha out of her mind. Yet, in doing so, it felt all the more devastating to see her in the flesh once more. Rio wasn’t sure if she was imagining things, but Agatha looked even more beautiful tonight. She wore a dark green suit with a black blouse. A gold necklace glinted at her neck, and her hair fell in loose curls around her. Rio had never wanted someone as badly as she did Agatha in that moment.

Rio would have stood there, staring at her all night, but then James brushed past her, exclaiming, “Is the world ending? That’s the only explanation for you being early for once.”

“My meeting ended early, and traffic was suspiciously light,” Agatha replied, rolling her eyes. “Trust me when I say I would have hidden in my car until you arrived, but Mother found me and insisted I come inside.”

“Dragged you in by the ear?” James teased. 

“Nearly.”

Agatha seemed so normal, except for one thing. She hadn’t looked at Rio once. She smiled and joked with James with an enviable ease, but not once had Rio seen those blue eyes focus on her. She hadn’t realized how often Agatha looked at her until she ignored her so completely. Despite being the one to distance herself first, Rio felt the loss acutely.

The only time Agatha let herself slip was when James made her drink without asking, handing it to her as he resumed his seat. Her eyes narrowed ever so slightly, staring at the drink in Rio’s hand, before they flicked back to James.

That was all Rio got. A flash of a glare.

As James and Agatha spoke, Rio began to feel invisible the same way she did when James and Evanora spoke. It made her ill to feel this way because of Agatha. Mainly, because she never wanted Agatha and Evanora to have any similarities in her mind. Agatha was better than that. And yet, it was impossible to deny the sensation of feeling very small, of feeling very insignificant.  

It was almost a relief when Evanora came out to inform them dinner was ready, and Rio couldn’t even begin to process how fucked up that was.

Naturally, that feeling couldn’t last. They were halfway through their entrées when Evanora asked, “So, Rio, have you given any more thought to having children?”

“Mother,” James said warningly. 

Across from Rio, Agatha went completely still, hands clenched around her silverware. To everyone’s surprise, she looked at Evanora and asked, “Eager to be a grandmother?” 

There was an unspoken again that Rio heard, even if she wasn’t supposed to know. She held her breath as Evanora and Agatha stared at each other in a silent battle of wills. Rio already knew how this would end and had to hide her smile when Evanora looked away first.

“Yes, I am,” Evanora said primly. “You’ll understand one day.”

Agatha let out a quiet, disbelieving laugh, but she said nothing else. The rest of dinner was eaten in a tense silence. 

When it was over, Evanora asked to speak with James in the office, and Agatha disappeared as soon as they left. Rio sat there for as long as she could, but soon enough, the maids were inching out from the kitchen, ready to begin cleaning.

Rio thought about wandering the house, but all it reminded her of was the tour Agatha had given her. She wandered outside instead, only to find that this was where Agatha had gone. She stood among the flowers, bathed in moonlight, and Rio felt her breath catch. Although she knew it would be better to turn around and go back inside, Rio kept walking. She stopped a few feet away from Agatha, purposefully looking out at the rest of the garden instead of her. From the corner of her eye, Rio could see that Agatha was smoking a cigarette. The smell made Rio itch for one, but she knew better than to ask.

It was Agatha who broke the silence first, saying, “The least you could have done was end things properly.” She glanced at Rio with half-lidded eyes. “I guess I expected too much to think you wouldn’t take the coward’s way out.”

The remark hit her just as Agatha intended, and Rio stumbled back as if it physically struck her. “What did you want me to say?” Rio asked. As hurt as she was, she could still feel guilt and rage churning inside her too. “Agatha, I can’t do this anymore? Agatha, this is wrong? Agatha, what the fuck were we thinking?” Rio’s voice rose with every question, vitriol fueling every word. “Are you upset that I didn’t say it, or are you upset that I ended things at all?” Rio asked. When Agatha said nothing, Rio glared at her. Trying for a reaction now, she said, “Did you really think it was going to last? What if someone found out?”

Again, Agatha said nothing, and Rio wanted to scream for her to at least look at her. To treat her like she actually saw her, to remind Rio that someone knew the real her fucking existed. 

When Agatha spoke, it was quiet and measured. “I never made myself hide,” Agatha said. “All my life, I never let myself be in the closet, not even when my parents tried to shove me in there and lock the door.” Agatha finally looked at her, and Rio felt like she’d been swallowed whole. She couldn’t remember Agatha ever looking at her with such disgust and loathing. “How do you think it felt being your dirty little secret? Do you think I enjoyed that?”

“It is not just because you’re another woman, Agatha,” Rio hissed. “You were sleeping with your brother’s wife."

“And you were fucking your husband’s sister.”

Rio wasn’t sure when they got so close, but suddenly, she realized that she was standing just inches from Agatha, breathing hard, with her hands clenched in fists at her sides. This close, Rio could see that her blue eyes were a tumultuous storm, and even then, Rio wanted to drown herself in them.

Agatha looked away first, walking away. “Good-bye, Rio.”

It sounded too final. Rio spun to stop her, only to find James standing in the doorway. He looked worried, eyebrows furrowed, as he looked between Rio and Agatha. How much had he heard?

“Everything okay?” James asked, and Rio nearly collapsed in relief. Nothing. He heard nothing. 

“Doing great!” Agatha said brightly.

James gave his sister a look, but he said nothing. He only shook his head. He looked back at Rio and asked, “Ready to go home?”

Agatha’s jaw clenched for a brief moment. She didn’t look at Rio again.

James offered a smile and tucked his hands into his pockets. He hadn’t looked away from Rio once.

Rio sighed. “Yeah, let’s go home.”

The car ride home was quiet except for a brief exchange where James asked tentatively, “What did Agatha say to you? You seem upset.”

“Nothing,” Rio said immediately.

“I can talk to her–”

“No,” Rio said sharply. She pinched her nose when she saw James’s hurt expression. “I’m sorry. I didn’t mean to snap. It’s just stupid.”

“Are you sure?” James asked as the car arrived at their apartment. 

“I’m sure,” Rio said firmly. They stood in front of their building, and Rio wrapped her arms around herself. “Go up without me. I’ll be in later.”

“Where are you going?” James asked.

“I just need to clear my head,” Rio said, being honest this time. After tonight, she needed to just get away from anyone with the last name Harkness. “I won’t be out too late.”

James looked like he wanted to protest, but after a moment, he sighed and said, “Just be careful. Call if you need someone to pick you up.” Rio offered him a faint smile and allowed James to press a kiss to her cheek. She watched him go up the steps and waited until he was inside before she called a car.

It’d been months since she’d been out, but there was always one bar Rio could rely on. 

Pancho’s looked exactly as Rio remembered it, like a time capsule from another era with all of its wood and vintage decor. Rio slid onto a bar stool off to the side and ordered a whiskey. She made her way through two more rounds, admittedly wallowing about what a disaster her life had become. It sounded like the beginning of a really bad joke. A lesbian marries a man and has an affair with her sister-in-law. Rio wondered what the punch line would be. 

The bartender came around again, a pretty blonde with a playful smirk. Carol, Rio remembered from past visits. She owned the place with her wife. Waving her empty glass, Rio informed her, “I’m a mess.”

“Aren’t we all?” Carol replied. She plucked the glass from Rio’s grasp and poured her some more whiskey.

Rio gave her a wide, drunken grin in thanks and said, “I’m, like, really a mess.”

“Well, go on then,” Carol said, chuckling. She leaned against the back counter and folded her arms across her chest. “Tell me all about your woes. You don’t come in as often as you used to, so I could use the update anyways.”

“I’m married,” Rio said, holding up her left hand.

Carol’s eyes widened. “Oh, shit.”

“To a man.”

Carol let out a low whistle and grabbed the bottle of whiskey again. “Something tells me we’re going to need a lot more than this,” Carol sighed.

Several drinks later, Rio stumbled her way through a retelling of her failure of a marriage, cheating and all. She was vaguely aware of the fact that she shouldn’t be telling a stranger this in a public bar, but Rio was too far gone to care. Besides, no one in a bar like this would know or care about the Harknesses. 

By the time the bar was closing, Carol had Rio’s arm slung around her shoulders as she helped her out to her car. Rio tried to tell her that she could get herself home, but Carol wouldn’t listen. After the fifth try, Rio just sighed and slumped in the passenger seat, mumbling her address to Carol.

Rio dozed off on the way, only waking up when Carol dragged her out of the car to help her up to her apartment. She felt bad. It was nearly three in the morning, and Carol had a wife waiting for her at home. Rio made a promise to herself to go back and leave a good tip. 

After a few minutes of knocking, James opened the door with his hair sticking up. He squinted at them for a moment before he sighed and murmured, “Oh, Rio. What happened?”

“She’s fine,” Carol said. “Just drunk. I think she was a little stressed.”

A wild understatement, and Rio tried to say so. Before she could though, Carol passed her off to James. The two of them were talking about her, Rio was pretty sure. James was thanking Carol for bringing her home safely, and Rio wanted to roll her eyes. She wasn’t a child.

Once Carol was gone, Rio leaned against James and said, “I need to tell you something.”

Rio ignored the tiny part in the back of her mind that was screaming. She was just so tired. She didn’t want to do this anymore. She wanted James to know. She told Carol, and the world hadn’t ended. That meant she could tell James too, right?

“Tomorrow, Rio,” James said as he guided her to her bedroom. “You are in no state to be telling me anything.”

“It’s important, James,” Rio tried.

“I’m sure it is, but it can wait until tomorrow.”

“But what if–” Rio stopped herself, a brief moment of clarity jolting through her. It came to her as she saw a framed photo of James and Agatha together. It was the two of them at James’s college graduation. They looked young. They looked happy. 

Rio bit her lip. She was tired. She was so fucking tired, but she was also scared. She was terrified. What the hell was she doing? There was no guarantee James’s kindness would continue after finding out what she’d done and who she really was.

James frowned. “Rio?”

Rio’s voice was small as she asked, “What if I’m too afraid to tell you tomorrow?” 

James’s smile was gentle as he ran a hand over Rio’s hair. The touch felt weird. She didn’t dislike it. At least, she didn’t think she did. It just felt unnatural. It was different from how Agatha would touch her hair. It felt wrong.

“That’s okay,” James told her. “You can tell me another day.”

Even through her drunken haze, Rio didn’t think she would. As it processed further for her that she wasn’t in the safe anonymity of Pancho’s anymore , that if she told she’d be ruining Agatha’s relationship with James, Rio knew she couldn’t tell the truth. 

The confession that had been on the tip of her tongue was swallowed once more, sinking deep inside Rio.

Chapter End Notes

i have been looking forward to writing that conversation between agatha and rio since i started planning this fic so i hope it emotionally destroyed you a little the way it did for me :)

Chapter 11

Chapter Summary

Just like that, it became clear to Rio the kind of man James was.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

When Rio woke up, it was to a pounding headache that was bad enough to rival the hangover she had on her wedding day. She tried to sit up, only for the whole room to spin and nausea to wash over her. Rio practically fell out of bed trying to get the bathroom, and as it was, she barely made it to the toilet.

After throwing up, Rio slumped against the wall and cursed herself for drinking so much. She was getting too old for this shit. 

Rio dozed off again, and when she woke up again, she forced herself to stand up and shower. The hot water helped, making her a little more alert and washing off the grime from the previous night. The headache stayed though, as did the exhaustion. 

Since it was Saturday, Rio didn’t have anything planned, so she changed into sweatpants and an oversized t-shirt before she padded out to the kitchen. To her surprise, James was there, dressed similarly to her, reading something on his phone. When he noticed her, he set down his phone and asked, “How are you feeling?”

 “Like shit.”

James laughed and stood up. “Here, sit. I’ll get you some coffee.”

Rio didn’t argue and sank into one of the chairs. She rested her head on her folded arms on the table, eyes lazily following James around the kitchen as he poured coffee into a mug. He placed it in front of her and resumed his seat. “Thanks,” Rio mumbled. She sat up just enough to drink the coffee. 

The two of them sat in comfortable silence for a few minutes while Rio sipped at her coffee. When she was done, James asked, “Do you want to talk about it?”

Rio peered down at her mug and gave a small shake of her head. “I’m sorry you had to see that,” she said.

“You’re allowed to drink,” James told her. “I guess I’m just more worried that I’m the thing that drove you to drink that much.”

“No, it’s not you,” Rio said. Not entirely at least. She bit her lip, trying to decide how to phrase this. “I guess I’m just not adjusting to all the changes in my life as well as I thought I was.”

James nodded thoughtfully then asked, “When’s the last time you talked to your parents? You’re close, right?”

Rio opened her mouth, but she hesitated. When was the last time they spoke? The sudden realization made her queasy all over again. It used to be that Rio couldn’t go a day without getting a text or call from her parents.

“Give them a call,” James said. He stood up and stopped by her chair. He placed a hand on her shoulder, squeezing gently. “While you do that, I’m going to go out and buy some food, so we can just relax on the couch today. How’s that sound?”

“Don’t you have things to do?” Rio asked. He always had things to do.

“I rearranged things,” James shrugged, as if it wasn’t a big deal. Rio knew better though. She knew from her father exactly how difficult it could be to move meetings around last minute. “This is more important. I should be a better husband to you, and that includes helping you get over the worst hangover I’ve ever seen.”

Rio laughed softly, “You just want an excuse to lay around all day,” It was sweet of him, and Rio couldn’t help but imagine how lucky another woman would be to have a doting husband like him.

“Well, that’s definitely a bonus,” James winked. He patted her shoulder and pulled away. “Call your parents. I’ll be back in about two hours.”

Rio didn’t appreciate the way James advised her like he knew better than her, but she had to admit that it also wasn’t a bad idea. With the whirlwind of the new marriage and everything with Agatha, Rio had lost track of how long it’d been. Then again, her parents hadn’t reached out either, and that stung in a way that felt like a knife between her ribs.

Migrating to the couch, Rio found her phone and called her mother.

The phone rang a few times before Paola picked up and said, “Hello? Rio? How are you doing?” Rio must have said something because then Paola started going on and on in a way she used to find so annoying but now found comforting. At some point, Paola slipped into Spanish as she spoke, and Rio let the language wash over her, shutting her eyes. 

It didn’t matter that Paola was telling her gossip about distant aunt. For Rio, hearing her mother’s voice in a language that hadn’t been spoken to her in weeks was the balm Rio needed right now. She let Paola go on and on, almost lulling herself to sleep, until Paola said, “But really, Rio. How are you? How are things going with James and Evanora?”

And Agatha, Rio wanted to add. She bit her lip instead. “It’s okay,” Rio said. “I miss you.”

There was a pause, and Rio wondered if she hung up when Paola sniffled. “I miss you too,” Paola whispered. “You can come home and visit any time, you know that, don’t you? I know you’re married now, but you’re still our little girl.”

Rio wanted to ask why she hadn’t told her any of this sooner, but she also wasn’t sure if she would have gone. The last few weeks had lessened some of the resentment that blistered beneath the surface. Rio could focus less on the fact that her parents married her off and more on the fact that she missed them despite that. 

“Soon,” Rio said, feeling her throat close up as she fought back tears of her own. “I’ll come soon.” She heard the apartment door open and hastily wiped at her eyes. “I have to go, but I’ll call again soon, okay?” Or, maybe, you can call me?

“I love you,” Paola said. 

Rio let out a shaky breath. “I love you too.” She hung up the phone just as James walked into the living room, arms laden with take-out and junk food. Rio knew she probably looked like even more of a wreck after that phone call, but James merely asked, “What do you want to watch?”

For the rest of the day, the two of them sat on the couch, watching nature documentaries and snacking on all of the food James got for them. Sometimes, they talked, commenting on things that were happening, but they also just sat in silence for a lot of it. Every so often, James would excuse himself to take a call, but he’d always come back with a smile and a joke.

A few hours later, on screen, a line of ducklings followed their mother. James pointed and said, “Did you know Agatha used to follow me around like that when we were younger?”

Rio couldn’t imagine Agatha following James around the way younger siblings usually did, all wide-eyed and admiring and trying to be just like them. The skepticism must’ve been abundantly clear on her face because James laughed and said, “I mean, she used to follow me and try to do everything I did. Just to prove she could.”

That sounded more like her. Rio smiled and asked, “Like what?”

“All sorts of things,” James said. He laughed softly and said, “Once, I climbed a tree, and I told her she couldn’t. She was too small.”

“And let me guess,” Rio said knowingly. “She climbed the tree.”

“To this day, I have no idea how she managed it,” James said, shaking his head. “She was always stubborn. Braver than I ever was too.” His smile turned shy, and his cheeks turned pink. Rio wondered what could make him so embarrassed when James admitted, “Agatha actually used to defend me a lot when we were kids.”

“She did?” Rio said. She couldn’t help but smile, charmed by the image. She imagined the primly dressed girl she saw in their family portrait with Agatha’s fire, yelling at others. “Did kids pick on you?”

“I’ve always been a pretty easy-going guy,” James explained. “And when I was a kid, well, I’d have picked on me too. Well-dressed, from a well-to-do family, but incapable of standing up for himself. I’d just let the taunts come and go. Agatha though?” James’s grin was fond as he chuckled. “It didn’t matter that she was younger and smaller than everyone else. She’d yell at them all the same. She’d bite too.”

Rio let out a startled laugh at that, but she could see it so easily. If they had known each other as children, would Agatha have defended her like that too? Would they have gotten along? It was hard to imagine a child as headstrong and exuberant as Agatha would have liked a child as quiet and reserved as Rio. 

“I’m sure everyone was relieved when she grew out of the biting and stuck to fighting with words,” Rio said, thinking about Agatha’s career as a lawyer.

James’s easy smile flickered though, and he said, “No, uh, she used to fight every so often in middle and high school, physically at least, but fighting with words sometimes landed her in more trouble than the fist fights.”

“The two of you must have been at the same school often,” Rio remarked, watching him carefully. “Even when…” She stopped herself. She wasn’t supposed to know about Nicky. She licked her lips and continued, “Even when she gained a reputation as a teenager.”

“I love my sister,” James said, and Rio was reminded of the way James had said this about his mother. Like a reminder. “And I did my best to stop people when I heard them talking shit about her at school, but…” James let out a heavy sigh, and for the first time, Rio saw the kind of exhaustion she saw reflected on her own face when she looked in a mirror.

“I used to really resent Agatha,” James told her quietly. “By the time we were both in high school, every time she fucked up, it felt like it was up to me to fix it. Or, I guess not fix it, but to do something to distract everyone from it.” James’s jaw clenched, and Rio could see it in his eyes that he was lost in another time. “Agatha would get caught fucking someone’s daughter in the school restroom, so I had to get the highest test score in Calculus. Agatha would get caught getting high at the park, so I had to win class president.” James sank fully into the couch and ran a hand over his face. His voice was small and vulnerable as he said, “I just felt like I had to be perfect all the time to make up for the fact that she wasn’t.”

It was so easy for Rio to compare James to Agatha, and every other time, Rio always favored Agatha, but in this moment, Rio couldn’t help but wholeheartedly sympathize with James.

Although Rio had no siblings of her own, she understood the need to be as good as possible, to fight for your family’s reputation. Just like that, it became clear to Rio the kind of man James was. He was a good guy, yes, but he also really wanted to be the perfect guy. He was kind and patient and caring, and while Rio had no doubt that was his personality, she could also tell that he pushed himself to fully inhabit those traits because that was what would help him and his family. That was the kind of man, the kind of husband he was supposed to be. 

He was so different from Agatha. 

Agatha reminded Rio of a finely honed knife, beautiful but dangerous with sharp edges. One wrong move and you’d cut yourself. Meanwhile, James was smooth metal, polished and shiny and something to admire. No serious harm to others but constantly in need of buffing. A constant maintenance required to appear unobtrusive and likeable. 

James wanted a perfect life after years of struggling to maintain the facade of one. He expected everything to fall into place if he just did as he was supposed to do. 

He wasn’t perfect though and neither was Rio. Things would be so much easier if all Rio wanted was to be perfect. If only she cared about that, then maybe she’d be able to ignore all of her other desires.

Rio felt a headache coming on. Even as she sympathized with James on the pressure to be perfect, she also couldn’t help but respect Agatha for her choice to be unabashedly who she was. 

Unaware of how long she’d been silent, Rio startled when James forced a laugh and said, “Sorry, I didn’t mean to dump all of that on you.”

“No, it’s fine,” Rio hurried to say. She reached out and squeezed his hand. “I’m glad you felt like you could tell me that.” She offered a hesitant smile. “And I get it. Having to do well in, well, everything. My parents were always telling me I had to be the best.”

“Yeah,” James sighed. “Nothing less.” His smile was tired but genuine as he said, “Thanks, Rio.” 

Maybe Rio would never love James the way she was supposed to, but maybe she would love him in another way. The way you do a comrade in arms, someone you love because no one else will understand what you’re going through except them. After all, who better to understand this marriage than the one she was married to?

The two of them fell into another comfortable silence when their doorbell rang. They shared a look. However, they both looked just as surprised as the other.

“Expecting someone?” James asked, standing up.

“No,” Rio said. She got up to follow. “Are you?”

When they opened the door, the last person Rio expected stood on the other side. Agatha wore a false smile that only partially distracted from the fact that her eyes were watery and red. She looked like she just came from work in a rumpled suit. 

“Hi,” Agatha said lightly. “Mind if I come in?”

Rio and James shared a look, but they both stepped back to let her in. Agatha brushed past them as soon as the path was cleared. James walked after his sister, asking why she was here, and Rio just stood there for a moment, trying to remember to breathe.

apologies for the lack of agatha in this one but i really wanted to shed some light on her relationship with james

the next chapter will have a lot more of her!

Chapter 12

Chapter Summary

“Your brother doesn’t deserve this,” Rio said, but she didn’t push Agatha away. Instead, her hands curled around the smooth fabric of her blouse. “It’s cruel.”

“And what do I deserve?”

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

As she made a pot of tea, Rio was relieved to find that she wasn’t the only one confused by Agatha’s sudden appearance. She could hear the soft murmur and James and Agatha speaking in the living room, but she doubted it was about why Agatha was here. Rio sighed and stared down at the kettle. 

Her last conversation with Agatha echoed in her mind, and Rio gripped the edge of the counter. She’d never forget the disgust Agatha had directed at her. Not that it had been unwarranted, but that made it all the more shameful. A dirty little secret, she’d said. Was that really how she’d felt? Was that how Rio had felt? 

Rio ran a hand through her hair, thinking. There were layers of shame and guilt and fear when it came to being with Agatha, but at the same time, there was also a sense of pride and joy that Agatha had chosen her of all people. There was something heady and intoxicating about that. There was something that kept Rio coming back against all common sense. But then, the shame and guilt and fear had won in the end. Rio had let them win.

Would Agatha even bother to look at her now?

When the tea was ready, Rio had no other reason to keep hiding. She sighed and loaded up the tray, carrying it out to the living room. The conversation abruptly ended when she entered the room, and Rio tried not to read too much into it. 

It was only once the tea was served and Rio was sitting that James asked, “So, Agatha, what brings you here tonight?”

“What, I can’t visit my darling brother and sister-in-law?” Agatha replied with a dazzling smile that might have distracted Rio, if not for the fact that her hand shook ever so slightly as she lifted her mug to drink from. 

“Agatha,” Rio said softly. She didn’t expect Agatha to look at her, but when she did, Rio’s breath caught. There wasn’t the harshness there from last time. If Rio didn’t know any better, she would have said there was fear. Rio swallowed. “Agatha, what’s going on?”

Agatha held out for thirty more seconds before her shoulders slumped. “It’s Nicky,” she said. At the mention of her son, James looked sharply at Rio, but Agatha waved a hand and said, “She knows, James.”

“She knows?” James repeated, looking between them.

“Rio saw us at the hospital together,” Agatha explained. “I figured I could trust your wife with my secret.”

James nodded, accepting this easily. Meanwhile, Rio couldn’t help but recall the day Agatha told her this. It certainly hadn’t been because of her marriage to James. She said nothing though. If anything, she was surprised James knew. She would have thought Agatha would keep this from him, considering that he seemed closer to Evanora, more craven to her whims. Evanora clearly knew nothing though, so maybe Rio should give him more credit. 

“What’s wrong with Nicky?” James asked. “Is he okay?” 

“He’s fine,” Agatha assured him, “but his adopted mother is moving back to Italy in a few months.” She paused, letting that sink in for them. “He’s only sixteen, so he should go with her, but he wants to stay.” She opened her mouth and closed it, pressing her lips together. She took a deep breath. “I want him to stay,” Agatha said quietly. 

“Then he’ll stay,” James said, like it was just that easy. Immediately, Rio caught a glimpse of James and Agatha as children, just as James described them. James, desperate, eager, obligated, to be Agatha’s protector and savior. “We’ll figure something out.”

Agatha smiled, but there was something saddened about the expression. “I’m glad you said that,” Agatha said. “I need your help.” She fiddled with her mug for a moment before she said, “I want guardianship of Nicky, so he can stay here. His adopted mother is okay with it, but you know that our mother is going to try and stop this as soon as she finds out that I’m doing this. I need your connections so that this goes through quickly and quietly.”

“Done,” James said immediately, and even Agatha looked surprised by his easy agreement. He sighed and reached out, placing a hand on Agatha’s wrist. “I never liked that they did that,” James told her. “You didn’t deserve that, and neither did Nicholas. I’ll do whatever I can to make sure you don’t get separated again.”

Agatha looked away. She looked like she was holding back tears, but her voice was steady as she whispered, “Thank you, James.”

“Let me make some calls right now,” Jame said, standing up. “Better to get this started now rather than later.” He held out a hand with a raised brow. “I assume you brought all of the necessary paperwork?” Agatha bit the inside of her cheek, but she reached into her bag and procured a manila folder for him. “Presumptuous,” James teased.

“Prepared,” Agatha corrected. She gave James a playful smile and said, “I knew you couldn’t say no to me.”

“No,” James said, a heaviness crossing his face for the briefest moment. “I can’t.” He took the folder and excused himself to the office, explaining this would take a while. 

After he left, Rio and Agatha sat in silence, not even looking at each other. It only took five minutes before Agatha stood up and began to pace. Rio watched her go, back and forth, back and forth, for while until she finally called out, “Agatha.”

Her voice made Agatha stop immediately. Her back was to her, but Rio could see the tension that ran through her entire body. Rio slowly stood up and walked up behind her. Before she could talk herself out of her, Rio ran her fingers through the ends of Agatha’s hair. Agatha relaxed minutely, but what was even more telling was the quiet sigh that left her lips.

“It’s going to be okay,” Rio told her. 

Agatha turned slowly, half-angled towards Rio with an unreadable expression on her face. “You don’t know that,” she said.

“I don’t,” Rio agreed, “but I can hope.” She let another silence fall between them for a minute before she tentatively said, “I’m also sorry.” Just like that, the tension snapped back into Agatha’s frame. Rio hurried to add, lowering her voice, “I was wrong to just stop texting you. I should have at least sent you a message or done it face-to-face.”

“Thank you,” Agatha said after a moment. “For apologizing.”

“The least I could do,” Rio shrugged.

Agatha faced her fully now. She lifted a hand to Rio’s face, and when Rio didn’t stop her, she cupped her cheek. Rio let out a shaky breath and leaned into the touch. Agatha’s palm was warm against her cheek, and Rio found herself craving more of Agatha’s hands on her body. She held still though, scared to move and make Agatha pull away.

“Do you miss me?” Agatha asked. Although her voice was low, almost emotionless, there was a hunger to her gaze that made Rio feel as though she’d been stripped bare. 

“Don’t make me say it,” Rio said.

Agatha’s other hand came up to cradle Rio’s face, and Rio gasped as Agatha brought their faces closer together. “Say it,” Agatha whispered. “You owe me this.”

Rio’s heartbeat felt thunderous in her chest as Agatha stared at her, almost as if she might be able to force the words from her lips with her eyes. It wasn’t necessary though. The words spilled from her lips so easily. 

“I missed you.”

Rio watched as Agatha’s eyes flicked down to her lips. When Agatha leaned in then hesitated, Rio didn’t stop her. It was only when Agatha leaned in that a second time that Rio regained enough sense to stop her, throwing her hands up between them. It would be so easy to let Agatha kiss her right now, but she couldn’t. Not here. Not like this. Not with James just in the other room.

“Your brother doesn’t deserve this,” Rio said, but she didn’t push Agatha away. Instead, her hands curled around the smooth fabric of her blouse. “It’s cruel.”

“And what do I deserve?” Agatha replied. She was so close now that Rio could feel the warmth of her breath against her lips and see the traces of green in her eyes. 

“Better than this.” Better than me.

“Rio–”

“You aren’t my dirty little secret,” Rio told her. She forced herself to take a step back, and when Agatha’s hands fell away from her, she felt cold all over. “I don’t want you to be one.”

“What am I then?” Agatha asked. She looked just as thrown off by this as Rio felt. Her chest rose and fell faster than normal, and Rio wanted so badly to press her hand over her heart and feel its rapid beat. 

“I don’t know,” Rio said. “I don’t know what we can be without…” Rio bit her lip. She tried again, “It’s not about the–” Her cheeks flushed, and Rio’s gaze dropped. “I miss you, Agatha,” Rio said, hoping her emphasis will help her understand what she meant. “I miss talking to you.”

When Rio looked up again, Agatha’s expression was unreadable once more. “If you want something, say it, Rio.”

You. Rio sighed and said, “Is it stupid if I say I want to be friends?”

“Extremely,” Agatha said without missing a beat. She stared at Rio for a moment before she continued, “But lucky for you, I enjoy a bit of stupidity in my life. Keeps me entertained.”

Despite herself, Rio laughed. Deadpan, she said, “I’m glad I can amuse you.” Her smile faded a little as she looked at Agatha more closely. “Do you mean it though? We can be friends?”

“Well, we’re already family,” Agatha said with a shrug. Her eyes hadn’t met Rio’s again though. “We might as well be friends too.” Finally, she looked at Rio. She wore a half-smile as she did. “There are worse friends to have than you, I suppose.”

“Are you this nice to all of your friends, or am I getting special treatment?” Rio drawled sarcastically.

Agatha’s smile grew into a full grin. “Oh, don’t worry. All of my friends find me insufferable.”

“It’s true.”

At James’s voice, Rio stiffened, and Agatha’s smile grew strained. James joined them again in the living room, glancing between them curiously. “It’s nice to see the two of you getting along,” James said. Rio bit her lip while Agatha rolled her eyes. James handed Agatha the folder back and said, “I have some friends who’ve started the process already. They’ll get back to you by tomorrow with a date.”

“Thank you,” Agatha said. She reached out and squeezed James’s arm. “I mean it.”

“Anything for my favorite sister,” James teased. 

Agatha rolled her eyes and grabbed her bag. “Good night, James.” She shouldered her bag and glanced at Rio. “Good night, Rio.”

Rio stayed where she was while James walked Agatha to the door. When he came back, he wrapped a loose arm around her shoulders. “Everything good between the two of you now?” James asked, eyes still fixed on the door. 

“Yeah,” Rio nodded. She wondered how much James knew. He had to suspect something, but was it that he suspected? “We have different views on things,” she said, a vast understatement to their situation. “I think we’ve come to an agreement though.”

“Good,” James said. “Family has to stick together.”

Rio almost laughed. She was well aware of the fact. 

After that night, Rio found herself staring at her phone, waiting for a text message from Agatha. They agreed to be friends, but Rio wasn’t sure what that actually looked like. Not with Agatha, at least. With Alice, they texted and called every so often, meeting up whenever they had time. Rio couldn’t imagine doing the same with Agatha, texting her random thoughts or moments in her life. 

A week passed with nothing from Agatha, and Rio tried not to sulk. She knew she could text her first, but if she was being honest, she was afraid to. She wasn’t even sure what to say. Still, as the days went by, Rio resolved to text her if she didn’t hear from her by the end of the week.

It was Friday afternoon, and Rio was volunteering at the hospital when she saw Nicky. She’d seen him here and there, but they hadn’t done much more than wave the last few weeks. Today though, Nicky joined her on the gurney she was perched on, helping organize some papers for the nurses. 

“How’ve you been?” Rio asked.

“Okay,” Nicky shrugged. “School’s been tough lately, but it’s fine.”

Rio hummed and flipped through a few more files. “And everything else?”

Nicky didn’t answer immediately, eyeing Rio from the corner of his eyes. He fidgeted with his hands, but Rio let him stew in his silence. A few minutes passed before Nicky said, “I’m nervous.”

“You have a lot to be nervous about,” Rio said. She paused and looked at him, tilting her head. “Is there anything you’re really nervous about?”

“I’m not really worried about the guardianship,” Nicky admitted. “Agatha knows a lot of people.”

Rio’s lips twitched into a smile. “She does.”

Nicky gave a faint smile, but his hands hadn’t stopped fiddling with the volunteer badge he held. He fell silent once more, and Rio waited once more. He ducked his head, covering his face with his long strands. Nicky asked, “Is it bad that I’m nervous about living with her?”

“No,” Rio answered honestly. “You grew up without her for a long time, and even if you’ve known each other for years now, living with someone is a lot different than just spending time with them.” Rio nudged Nicky with her elbow and offered him a smile. “For what it’s worth though, I think the two of you will be just fine.”

“Thanks,” Nicky said. “Will I see you more once I move in with Agatha?”

Rio wasn’t expecting that. She blinked a few times before she said, “Um, I guess so? Why?”

“Agatha talks a lot about you, so I figured you must be over a lot,” Nicky explained innocently. 

“Agatha talks about me?” Rio asked dumbly. What did she say? It had to have been favorable for Nicky to expect her to be over often. What was there to say though? Did she still talk about her when Rio ignored her?

Nicky gave her a strange look and said, “Yeah. Why are you acting like that’s weird? Don’t you talk about your friends?”

“Of course,” Rio said, blushing. “I was–” She fumbled for an excuse for her surprise. Thankfully, before she had to come up with something, she spotted Agatha walking down the hall. “Agatha!” Rio called out, relieved. The other woman spotted them and gave a small wave.

“There you are,” Agatha said as she walked up to them. She ran a hand over Nicky’s head, brushing his hair out of his face. “I was looking all over for you.”

“Sorry,” Nicky said. “I was just talking to Rio.”

“I see that,” Agatha said. She glanced at Rio and offered her a quick smile. “Ready to go? Lilia’s expecting both of us for dinner.”

Nicky looked at Rio then he looked at Agatha. “Can Rio come?”

It was hard to tell who was more startled, Agatha or Rio. While Rio just gaped at the boy, Agatha said, “Nicky, I don’t think Lilia would like it if you just invited a stranger to your home.”

“Rio isn’t a stranger,” Nicky replied. “She’s your sister-in-law. It’s not like she’s some serial killer I found on the sheet.” He looked at Rio with a cheeky smile. “Are you a serial killer, Rio?”

Rio chuckled while Agatha gently cuffed him upside the head. “It’s also rude to invite another person without asking,” Agatha added.

“Lilia always cooks enough to feed an army,” Nicky continued to argue. “A big one too. What’s one more person?” 

Agatha shook her head, but she obligingly looked at Rio and wore a smile full of fond exasperation. “Well, it looks like there’s no changing his mind,” Agatha said. “Would you like to join us for dinner, Rio?” She hesitated before her smile softened. “It would be nice to catch up.”

When Agatha smiled at her like that, Rio knew she had no choice. “I’d love to,” Rio said. She hopped off the gurney and handed the papers off to the nurse. She thanked the nurse when she handed Rio’s purse to her from where she stored it in one of their cabinets. “Shall we?” Rio asked, turning back to the others.

The three of them walked out with Nicky in the middle, and as Rio listened to Nicky tell Agatha about his day, she couldn’t help but think that maybe she could get used to this. 

Just maybe, this friendship would work out after all. 

Chapter End Notes

the yearning is about to be dialed up to 11

Chapter 13

Chapter Summary

Over the course of the next month, Rio experienced what marriage might’ve been like in another life. Not to James, but to Agatha.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Over the course of the next month, Rio experienced what marriage might’ve been like in another life. Not to James, but to Agatha. 

That first dinner with Agatha, Nicky, and Lilia had felt like something out of a dream.

Rio was ushered into an apartment overflowing with trinkets and plants, and despite it being so vastly different from anything Rio had ever known, it felt like home. At the sound of the front door closing, Lilia came out of the kitchen. She stopped short when she noticed Rio, and Agatha was quick to introduce her.

Rio braced herself for annoyance at the unexpected guest, but Lilia merely hugged and said, “It’s lovely to meet you, Rio. These two talk about you all the time. Like mother, like son.”

Both Agatha and Nicky protested at this, wearing matching blushes. 

It should have felt strange, sitting at a table barely large enough to fit the four of them, but it felt cozy and easy. They ate homemade pasta and shared stories, mainly about Nicky growing up. Every so often, Rio or Agatha would share their own stories, and Rio had to hide a smile when Agatha so clearly redacted portions from her rebellious youth.

“You should come more often,” Lilia told her at the end of the night, shoving a container of leftovers into her hands. “You make them happy.”

Rio had stuttered a reply before she went out to her car. Agatha was waiting for her, leaning against her own car and doing something on her phone. When she noticed her, she pocketed it and stood up straight. “So, did they scare you off?” Agatha asked, mostly playful but Rio could hear the hint of trepidation in her voice as well.

“They’re great,” Rio said honestly. She looked over her shoulder and smiled softly. “They’re really great. They’re good people. They’re…” She sighed and shook her head. “They remind me of what it was like when I was younger. Before my father got into politics.” Agatha stepped closer and laid a hand on her arm, but Rio just kept talking, “I’m glad though. I’m happy for him, for both of you, that he got to grow up with someone like that.”

When Rio looked up, Agatha stared at her like she wanted to say something. The two of them stared at each other for a long moment before Agatha squeezed her arm and simply said, “I’m glad too.”

After that, Rio was invited to dinner two more times. For the first one, she lied to James and said she was going to meet Alice, but for the second one, she admitted she was going to see Agatha and Nicky. 

James looked hurt for a moment, but then he forced a smile and said, “I’m glad she feels like she can bring you around him.”

“Do you get to see him at all?” Rio asked hesitantly. 

“No,” was all James said. Rio left it at that. 

At these dinners, Rio let herself forget a little. She forgot that she was in a loveless marriage with one Harkness and halfway in love with the other. She was simply Rio, enjoying the company of an all-too-perceptive older woman, a sweet and curious boy, and Agatha, a woman who was becoming all the more interesting the longer Rio spent time around her. 

Rio had seen all kinds of sides of Agatha since meeting her, but she was completely different in the safety of Lilia’s apartment with Nicky. It was like all of her walls came down, leaving a doting, earnest mother. Agatha smiled easily and frequently at these dinners, laughing freely and teasing lovingly. It was all the more devastating when Agatha extended such affection from Nicky to Rio.

It wasn’t just Agatha, who already made things hard enough. It was Nicky and Lilia too, who made Rio’s head spin with possibilities just out of reach.

The dinners went like this: Agatha would tease her about being such a goody two-shoes, but Nicky would defend her, saying that both Agatha and Lilia told him he should follow the rules. It would inevitably lead to playful bickering between the two of them, and then either Rio or Lilia would cut in with a harmless anecdote about the kind of mischief Agatha got up to when she was younger. Agatha would complain they were working against her, but she always wore that delighted smile as she said this.

It was a family dinner, when it came down to it, and it was hard for Rio to remember that this wasn’t her family. Not really. 

The line was blurring for her, and it only worsened when she received a text from Agatha.

Agatha Harkness: Nicky and I are going to breakfast and the aquarium tomorrow. He’d like to know if you want to join us.

Rio stared at the text for a long time, unsure of what to do. Although she’d agreed to be friends with Agatha, finding some kind of solace in not losing her completely, she was beginning to feel a bit out of her depth. With every meeting, her feelings for Agatha grew, becoming something much more than the hopeless crush and need to escape that it’d been before.

There wasn’t any harm though if Rio didn’t act on it, right? James had hopes that Rio would fall in love with him one day, but he was under no delusions that she loved him now. The only person it would hurt if she continued this was Rio, who would be constantly reminded of what she could never have.

Rio Vidal: Sounds fun. When and where?

Agatha Harkness: We’ll pick you up at ten. 

Rio let out a sigh of relief when she read the time. James would be out of the apartment by then. It wasn’t that Rio wanted to hide her friendship with Agatha, but all she could remember was how James had looked when he realized that Agatha wanted Rio around Nicky but not him. It was something she should ask him about, but Rio was afraid of what he might say. 

In the end, Rio told James nothing. He didn’t expect her to tell her every detail of her day, letting her have her own life, just as he had his own life with work. 

As she got ready for the day, Rio put on jeans and a sweater to fend off the chill that was beginning to settle in. She twisted her hair up and put it in a clip, grabbing her purse just in time to see Agatha’s text to let her know she arrived. 

Rio half-expected to sit in the back, but the passenger seat was free. She slid into it with ease and turned halfway to tell Nicky, “Good morning.”

“Morning,” Nicky replied with a yawn. It was already late morning, but Rio supposed that for a teenager, ten in the morning was about the same as six in the morning. He offered a sleepy smile and said, “Ready to see some fish?”

“Can’t wait,” Rio said.

On the way to breakfast, Rio and Agatha talked about their respective weeks with Nicky piping in every so often. It felt so right, the three of them together, that Rio felt her heart give a traitorous skip when Agatha smiled at her. 

Rio expected breakfast to be at some posh restaurant, but to her surprise, they pulled up to a modest looking cafe that clearly wasn’t a chain. As she followed the other two inside, it occurred to her that it was probably more comfortable for Nicky to go to places like this, not to mention safer where it was less likely for someone to recognize Agatha.

As they sat down at the table, Rio and Agatha on one side and Nicky on the other, Nicky folded his hands in front of him and looked right at Rio. Solemnly, as if it were a matter of life or death, Nicky asked her, “Pancakes or waffles?”

A startled laugh escaped Rio’s lips. She hadn’t expected that. She glanced at Agatha and said, “Is he serious?”

Agatha smirked and shrugged, “It’s a very important question, Rio.”

“It’s a dumb question,” Rio said, and for a moment, Nicky looked hurt and Agatha murderous. However, Rio continued, saying, “But only because the answer is obviously waffles.”

Agatha’s shoulders relaxed while Nicky laughed, saying, “I knew you’d be on my side! Agatha prefers pancakes.”

“You do?” Rio raised an eyebrow.

“They’re better,” Agatha insisted, and to Rio’s utter amusement, she was earnest in her defense. “They’re fluffier and easier to eat too.”

“Waffles have that nice crisp to them though,” Rio argued. “They can still be fluffy too. Plus, they have the perfect wells to hold your syrup.”

“Agatha doesn’t eat her pancakes with syrup,” Nicky informed her.

Rio turned her body to Agatha fully now, staring at her in shock. “What the hell do you eat them with then?” 

“Honey,” Agatha said with a petulant sniff. “I’m not a heathen.”

Rio’s lips curled into a grin as she shook her head. She leaned across the table and whispered conspiratorially, just loud enough for Agatha to hear, “Don’t worry, Nicky. We’ll convert her to our side eventually.” Although she expected it, Rio still winced when Agatha elbowed her side. She rubbed the spot, glancing at Agatha who sipped her water innocently. 

“If it makes you feel any better, my preference may be a remnant from my childhood,” Rio offered. Nicky tilted his head curiously while Agatha paused. She glanced at Rio and slowly lowered her glass. Rio smiled and explained, “I ate a lot of frozen waffles growing up. It was quick and easy. Something to eat while I walked to school.”

“Maybe that’s it,” Nicky said thoughtfully. “I ate a lot of frozen waffles too. It was the weekends that Lilia would have time to cook a real breakfast.”

“Yeah, my mom too,” Rio smiled. 

While Rio and Nicky discussed the other kinds of foods they had growing up, Agatha watched them silently. She didn’t try to offer her own childhood memories, but Rio didn’t push and neither did Nicky. They both just let her listen to them, sharing stories about bread and beans and pasta and rice. 

When their food was finally served, their waitress gave them a sunny smile and asked, “Family day?”

While Rio flinched and Agatha stiffened, it was Nicky who smiled back and said, “Yeah. We’re going to the aquarium after this.”

“That sounds like a lot of fun,” the waitress said. She winked at Nicky and said, “You’re lucky that you don’t mind third-wheeling your sister and her girlfriend. I hate going to things with my brother and his wife.” Nicky’s eyes grew wide at this while Agatha choked on her coffee. The waitress startled and handed her a handful of napkins from her apron. “You okay?”

“Fine,” Agatha muttered, dabbing at her mouth.

“Thank you,” Rio cut in before anything else could happen. Her face felt warm at the assumption between her and Agatha, and she hoped it wasn’t obvious. “We’ll let you know if we need anything else.”

The waitress looked a little confused, but she nodded and left them alone. 

“People think Agatha’s my sister all the time,” Nicky told Rio.

“I’m not surprised,” Rio replied, and after that, she changed the topic.

As they had breakfast, Rio couldn’t help but feel grateful for the fact that Agatha agreed to be her friend. Her growing feelings aside, she really did enjoy the company. Although she saw Alice every so often, she was still busy. Agatha was busy too, but she was a better texter than Alice honestly, replying swiftly with snark to whatever Rio happened to send her that day. Since getting married, Rio had felt a kind of loneliness that pervaded her entire being, but spending time with Agatha kept it at bay.

When they got to the aquarium, Nicky ended up walking a few feet ahead of them, doing his own thing. Neither Agatha nor Rio minded, walking side-by-side and talking quietly as they walked through the various exhibits and tanks. 

Rio was embarrassed to admit that she only paid attention to the animals for half the time. The other half of the time, Rio couldn’t look away from Agatha. She was always beautiful, but she was especially stunning in the bluish glow from the tanks and the streaks of warmth from the sunlight that came through from the ceiling. Not only that, but as she always was with Nicky, Agatha was calm. She was at peace in a way she never was around the rest of her family, and Rio always savored the chance to see her like this.

As they observed one of the bigger habitats with various fish and sharks swimming around, Rio asked, “Do you mind spending your day like this? I mean, I know you’d do anything for Nicky, but do you mind doing stuff like this?”

“No,” Agatha said with a small shake of her head. She turned to look at her and asked, “Do you?”

Rio knew what she was asking. Did she mind doing this, having the time to do this, instead of having her old job? Rio missed being able to help patients so much some days that it made it hard to breathe, but she wasn’t ready to say that. Not here. Not like this. She merely said, “No, I love animals.”

Disappointment flickered through Agatha’s face before she managed a faint smile. She said, “Right, the squirrels.”

“You remembered,” Rio said in surprise.

Agatha’s cheeks pinkened as she turned back to the tank. She folded her arms over her chest and rocked back on her heels, saying, “It’s not every day someone tells you they want to catch and dissect a squirrel.” 

Rio felt warm all over at the thought of Agatha remembering such details about her. Then again, Rio remembered everything Agatha told her about herself too. 

Clearing her throat, Rio ducked her head and took a deep breath. She could feel the embarrassment emanating from Agatha and decided to take pity on her. Rio pointed to a shark swimming past them and said, “Did you know sharks can only swim forwards?”

“Really?” Agatha said. She glanced at Rio from the corner of her eyes. “Why?”

“Big heads,” Rio said. Agatha snorted, and Rio grinned, “No, really. It makes it hard for them to keep stable if they try to move backwards. Also, their pectoral fins just aren’t built for it.” Her smile widened at the way Agatha tilted her head, actually listening to her. Rio continued, “Some shark species also have to keep swimming or they die.”

Agatha scoffed, “Okay, now you’re just making up bullshit.”

“I’m not!” Rio exclaimed, laughing. “When they swim, water is pushed through their gills which gives them oxygen. No swimming, no water. No water, no oxygen. No oxygen, no shark.”

“How tiresome,” Agatha said. “Always moving forward, never stopping for a moment.”

Rio’s smile softened as she said, “Reminds me of someone.”

“Trying to say something?” Agatha replied, facing her fully and raising an eyebrow.

Rio shrugged innocently and said, “Well, people do compare lawyers and sharks a lot.”

“Mm, and the other stuff?”

Rio was about to deflect, but then she caught Agatha’s eyes. As blank as the rest of her face could be, Rio always found Agatha’s eyes painfully expressive, and the more time they spent together, the easier she found it was to read them. There was something insatiably curious in those bright eyes of hers, bluer than even that of the water that surrounded them and infinitely clearer. Almost icy by comparison, but there was also an undeniably warmth to them.

“I guess,” Rio began, shoving her hands into the pockets of her jeans. A part of her knew it was reckless to say this, but another part of her couldn’t help but want to give Agatha the same kind of comfort she so easily gave to Rio. Not to mention, there was something incredibly sad about the idea of Agatha never taking a break, of Agatha feeling like she could never take a break. Rio took a deep breath and let a shy smile spread across her face. She said, “I guess I just want you to know you can stop and rest. Just for a little while. At least, you can when you’re with me.”

When Agatha said nothing, Rio snuck a glance at her, only to find Agatha already looking at her. The curiosity was replaced by something much more tender, and Rio felt herself stop breathing for a moment. It was the kind of look Rio remembered seeing during those quiet moments in bed, in the lull before they were forced back into reality. 

Rio held her gaze for as long as she could, but it felt a little bit like drowning.

“We should keep going,” Rio said abruptly, forcing her eyes back to the aquarium. She licked her lips and internally cursed herself for ending the moment. “There’s still a lot to see. Like penguins. Love a penguin.”

Rio almost reached out to grab Agatha’s hand, but she stopped herself at the last moment. Her fingers brushed against Agatha’s wrist instead, and she swore she heard Agatha’s sharp intake of breath. Rio didn’t dare look at her though. She grasped the sleeve of Agatha’s jacket instead, pulling her in the direction Nicky was.

Not even for a moment did Rio allow herself to think about what all of this meant. For her, for Agatha, and especially not for the tenuous stasis that their lives seemed to be held in.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 14

Chapter Summary

Undoubtedly though, Rio’s favorite part of her weeks were the days she got to see Agatha alone.

Chapter Notes

i said i was going to take a break but now it's like my brain is entirely consumed by albatross???

maybe if i start posting again i can reverse psychology myself...

See the end of the chapter for more notes

As the weeks went on, Rio settled into a routine with the Harknesses.

Most days, Rio still went to the hospital to volunteer. There, she’d occasionally see Nicky, and the two of them would have lunch together if their schedules lined up. It was here that Rio got to see more of who Nicky was as a person, which turned out to be quiet, thoughtful, and kind. In a lot of ways, he was different from Agatha, but both of them had this unwavering loyalty about them that Rio couldn’t help but admire.

On Thursdays, Rio would have dinners at Lilia’s, a standing invitation that she took up most times. It remained an escape for Rio in many ways, this small, cozy apartment where all that seemed to matter was whether she could finish the monstrous serving Lilia gave her. 

On every other Friday, Rio would have dinner with James. It was called a “date” between the two of them, but Rio made it abundantly clear that she still only saw James as a friend. She waited for the day he’d tire of her insistence on friendship, but James only shook his head and said he was okay with being friends. 

“I hope we’ll fall in love one day,” James told her. He smiled and brushed some hair from his face. “I think you’re very easy to fall in love with, Rio.”

Rio hadn’t known what to say to that, so she had merely smiled and changed the subject. James let her. She wasn’t sure how to respond to that either.

Undoubtedly though, Rio’s favorite part of her weeks were the days she got to see Agatha alone. It wasn’t that she disliked Nicky or Lilia. There was actually something very special about being included in their time together. It was just different when it was just the two of them though. As gentle and soft Agatha was around Nicky, Rio also recognized her need to always be at her best around him. Not too sharp, not too rough.

Around just Rio, Agatha allowed some of her bite to show, throwing out caustic remarks and eye rolls that she would never allow herself to do around Nicky. It made Rio feel all warm, knowing Agatha felt comfortable enough to be herself around Rio. It felt like something. What? Rio wasn’t sure.

Although there’d been no more kisses, there had been lingering touches. Ones where neither of them seemed to be able to stop themselves from granting themselves a moment of hope. Rio’s favorite were when Agatha would brush Rio’s hair from her face, fingertips lingering against her cheek like she wanted to cup it. It made Rio want to lean in and press against her palm solidly, to let Agatha cradle her face gently like she used to.

On a morning where Agatha had no meetings and Rio had no plans, the two of them met at Agatha’s apartment to have breakfast together. Rio expected Agatha to just pick up some pastries or order food, but to her surprise, Agatha wore an apron to cook for them.

After pouring herself a cup of coffee, Rio perched herself on the counter and watched as Agatha moved around the kitchen. Apparently, Agatha had been craving a traditional American breakfast, so they were going to have bacon, eggs, and pancakes. The eggs were already cooked, and the bacon was in the oven. All that was left were the pancakes.

“Are you going to make them into shapes?” Rio asked playfully. “Can you make one into a heart or a rabbit?”

“Are you five?” Agatha retorted. She ladled the batter into the pan, letting it spread into a circle. When Rio made a noise of disappointment, Agatha sighed and said, “What if I flipped it?”

Rio raised a brow. “Like they do on TV?”

“It’s not that hard,” Agatha said. She lifted the pan, and without hesitation, she launched the pancake into the air. Rio was impressed for approximately three seconds before the pancake missed the pan, clipping the edge and landing on the stove. “Shit,” Agatha said. She set the pan down and hurried to clean up the pancake.

“Very impressive,” Rio deadpanned.

“I’m much better without an audience,” Agatha huffed.

“Sorry, should I close my eyes?” Rio teased. She did that, only to cover them with her hands as well. “Or like this. No peeking possible.” However, Rio did exactly that, spreading her fingers to watch Agatha ladle another spoonful of batter onto the pan. When Agatha only gave her an unimpressed look, Rio dropped her hands. She quietly watched as Agatha attempted another flip, and this one landed neatly back in the pan. As Agatha made another pancake, Rio asked, “How do you know how to cook so well?”

Agatha glanced at her. “Impressed?”

“That you can fend for yourself?” Rio smirked. “A little.”

Agatha smiled but didn’t answer. She made a few more pancakes, and Rio could see the way her mind seemed to be mulling over her answer. As she finished making the last of the pancakes, she handed Rio a plate.

It was only once they sat down that Agatha said, “I moved out when I was eighteen, so I had to learn then. I wasn’t…” Her face grew pinched. “My parents still paid for everything, but as soon as I went to college, I was gone, and I refused to live in a dorm, so I was in an apartment, all by myself. It was everything I wanted.” Despite her last sentence, Agatha didn’t sound like it’d been a very happy time for her at all. Rio remained silent, giving her the time to think. After a few bites of food, Agatha said, “It’s funny. I didn’t realize that my reputation would follow me all the way to college, but it did. Everyone knew exactly who I was, and no one wanted to talk to me because of it.” A wry smile came across her face. She lifted her mug and stared at Rio over the edge of it. “Well, unless they wanted to get into trouble.”

Rio thought about what Agatha told her, imagining a younger Agatha thinking she was finally free, only to be stuck in the same box their circle had always put her in. To say it sounded unfair was to put it lightly.

“I heard less about you when you went to college,” Rio said. Admittedly, Rio only heard about Agatha here and there growing up, but there’d still been a distinct decline when Rio was in high school.

“Because it wasn’t just me,” Agatha said with a shrug. “I was dragging down all the good boys and girls of the upper echelon with me. It’s harder to single me out in the gossip without letting it slip who else was involved, especially if it was their own children.”

That made a lot of sense. Trying to lighten the mood, Rio joked, “It sounds like you had a lot of fun in college.”

“Not really,” Agatha said. Her expression had gone pensive. She looked down at her food, saying, “People might have sought me out to have fun, but I wasn’t their friend. I was still the girl everyone’s parents warned them against.” There was a tense beat before Agatha looked up with a wan smile. “It’s lonely being a pariah.”

Rio swallowed at the present tense of her words.

Before she could say anything though, Agatha cleared her throat and said, “Sorry, you just asked about cooking.”

“I don’t mind,” Rio said softly, but she could sense Agatha’s retreat as if she’d physically closed a door between them.

“What about you?” Agatha asked. “What were your college years like?”

“Boring,” was all Rio could think to say. When Agatha gave her a thumbs down, even going as far as booing her, Rio laughed and insisted, “I’m serious. I didn’t really do much. I studied and I studied, and oh? You know? I studied.”

Agatha tilted her head, staring at Rio intently. “Really? That’s it?”

Rio hesitated. She didn’t like to talk about it, but she felt like she owed Agatha this after what she shared earlier. “I had a girlfriend in college,” Rio admitted.

“Oh?” 

Rio looked up from her coffee to find a peculiar look on Agatha’s face. If she didn’t know any better, she would have thought she looked jealous. 

“Yeah,” Rio said. She poked at her eggs, remembering all of the stolen kisses and panic attacks over being discovered. “We met in my second year, and we dated for almost two years. Eventually, she broke it off, but it was for the best.” It was painful to think about, even now. Rio pressed a hand to her chest, as if that might stave off the burning shame that lingered. “I loved her, but I was just too afraid to actually tell anyone about it, especially my parents. It would have never worked out.”

“I’m sorry,” Agatha said.

Rio could only laugh bitterly. “I’m sorry too.”

The rest of breakfast was finished in a stilted silence. Rio couldn’t help but think about her ex-girlfriend as she ate, where she was now and whether she was happy with another woman. She hoped so. She also wondered if Agatha was reliving her time in college too. It couldn’t be pleasant for her to think about. Still though, neither of them said anything.

After the dishes were cleared, Agatha announced, “Let’s go shopping. I still need a few things for Nicky’s room.”

“When’s he supposed to move in?” Rio asked, but she still walked over to the door and grabbed her coat. “The paperwork is pretty much done, right?”

“Two weeks,” Agatha said with a small but happy smile. “I’m nervous.”

“Are you sure you’re ready to handle all those teenage hormones?” Rio teased.

Agatha laughed and said, “Hopefully.”

It was a weekday, so the store wasn’t too crowded as Agatha grabbed a few smaller items for Nicky’s room. Rio had seen the steady progress of the room whenever she came over. It was simple but nice, and she imagined Nicky would have his own personal things to help make it feel a little more cozy. As they shopped around, Agatha talked about a break-up she caused while she was in college. Unlike earlier, she seemed happy to talk about this, but that probably had to do with the fact that it involved Agatha getting revenge on a girl who cheated off her test.

“It was so much fun when we were all at the next event together,” Agatha said. Her eyes were bright with glee. She was all but preening over her past victory, and it made Rio feel a ridiculous rush of fondness. “He was there with the girl he cheated with too. She was furious.”

“I wish I could’ve seen that,” Rio chuckled.

Agatha thought about it for a moment and said, “Maybe you did, but you didn’t know it.” She bumped her shoulder against Rio’s. “I’ve wondered, you know. Did we ever see each other growing up and just not realize it?”

Rio wasn’t sure whether to admit this or not, but after a moment, she said, “I saw you once when we were younger.” She bit her lip when Agatha whipped her head to look at her. She looked away, blushing, as she continued, “It was one of those awful garden parties, where it was hot but everyone acted like they weren’t melting. Some poor worker was fanning an old lady.” At this description, Agatha laughed and nodded. Rio smiled faintly. She said, “I was in some ugly pastel yellow dress my mom made me wear. I must have been thirteen or fourteen.” She could see Agatha do the math; she would have been about sixteen or seventeen, most likely just after having Nicky.

“Was I causing a scene?” Agatha asked lightly.

“Not at all,” Rio said. She closed her eyes briefly, imagining the scene. “You were sitting at one of the tables, wearing black. I thought you were so cool for that.” Agatha snorted, and Rio opened her eyes with a grin. She noticed Agatha was blushing, but she decided to be nice and not point that out. “What I really remember though was that you looked bored, like you wanted to be anywhere else but that party.”

“That was probably exactly how I was feeling,” Agatha said.

Rio nodded. “I remember being jealous too. I never let myself show how bored I was at those things.” She saw Agatha glance at her from the corner of her eye, but she stubbornly kept her eyes forward. “I used to smile so much it would make my cheeks hurt so much afterwards.”

Agatha opened her mouth then closed it. Her eyebrows scrunched together for a moment. When she finally spoke, she said, “I used to try and goad James into doing something uncouth at those things. I would offer him candy when we were younger, or my allowance when we got older. Whatever I could think of, really.”

“Did he ever take you up on such a great offer?” Rio laughed.

Agatha snorted, “Believe it or not, no.” 

Rio tried to imagine it. She pictured Agatha and James at the ages she saw them in the portrait at the estate. It was easy to imagine a younger Agatha trying to get James to do something he shouldn’t. It didn’t sound too dissimilar to them now, to be honest.

“You’re closer than I would’ve thought,” Rio said. She blinked a few times right after she said that. She hadn’t meant to say that out loud.

Agatha didn’t seem to notice her surprise, saying, “Don’t get it twisted. We hated each other a lot, especially when we were younger.”

“But?”

“But it was us versus them.”

The them were clearly their parents. Rio mulled over the idea of Agatha and James teaming up together. How long did it take for them to get to that point? What was the last straw before they realized they were better off together rather than against one another?

Rio could only imagine the amount of resentment Agatha felt towards James, and she already had an idea of some of the resentment James felt towards Agatha. Those feelings didn’t just disappear overnight, if they even went away at all. It would take something huge for someone to move past that. Rio wondered if it was Nicky that brought them together.

Glancing at Agatha, Rio waited to see if she would say anything, but she didn’t. Rio thought about asking, but Agatha had already shared so much with her today. She didn’t want to push her too far. Today was a good day so far. 

After paying for everything, the two of them decided to head back.

As Rio followed Agatha back into her apartment, her phone buzzed with a phone call. She fished it out of her pocket, only to stare at it in surprise. It was James. He never called her. Shutting the door behind her, she kicked off her shoes and answered the call. 

Vaguely, Rio was aware of Agatha saying something about ordering dinner in the kitchen. 

“Hey, James. Is everything–”

“Are you cheating on me?”

Chapter End Notes
