Chapter 15

Chapter Summary

Was this how it was going to be from now on? Putting on a show to make this loveless marriage seem flourishing?

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

There was a strange ringing in Rio’s ears. She opened her mouth, but she couldn’t form any words. Shock flooded her senses, rendering her dumb. Her wedding ring suddenly felt cold against her skin.

He couldn’t know. There was no way. It’d been over for months now. What was there to even discover? There was no proof, no evidence, no possible way for James to know that Rio had been with Agatha. 

Rio wracked her brain, trying to think if she left anything at Agatha’s, but that didn’t make any sense. James never came over to Agatha’s. When would he have had the opportunity to notice anything was amiss? There shouldn’t be any reason to suspect anything either. They had dates every other week, for god’s sake. 

Finally, Rio had the sense to choke out, “What the hell are you talking about?” When James didn’t answer immediately, Rio felt her face grow hot. She’d gotten her act together. She’d stopped. She’d given up the one thing that made her feel better to respect their marriage. How dare he accuse her of this now. “Why the hell would you ask that, James?” Rio snapped.

Agatha appeared in the doorway so quickly, you would have thought Rio called her name. Her eyebrows were drawn together. She took a step forward then stopped herself.

“I was anonymously sent photos of you,” James explained tersely. “You’re coming and going from the same apartment for weeks, Rio.” He sighed so heavily that it was loud even over the phone. “It’s not anywhere near convincing or damning, but it’s enough to make others question us. It could be a rumor that spirals quickly if there’s even a shred of truth to it.”

“Well, there isn’t!” Rio exclaimed. “I don’t know what apartment you’re looking at, but I am not cheating on you.”

Across from her, Agatha tensed, arms wrapped around herself. A distinct hunted look crossed her face as she only heard half of the conversation.

“Send me the photos,” Rio demanded. “Show me where I’m supposedly cheating on you, and I’ll tell you whose apartment it is.” 

James sighed again. His voice was low and condescending as he said, “This only works if we’re honest with each other, Rio.”

“I know that,” Rio said. She barely held back a snarl. “Send the photo.” This was the rudest she’d ever spoken to him. This was the closest they’d ever been to a fight, actually. They never talked about anything serious enough to argue over something. 

Rio’s head was spinning at the accusation, so when she received the photo, only to see Agatha’s apartment, the very apartment she was in at the moment, staring back at her, Rio laughed hysterically. 

This only made Agatha more concerned, who finally walked closer and laid a hand on Rio’s arm.

“Are you kidding me?” Rio said, pressing the phone back to her ear. “James, do you seriously not know whose apartment that is?” She felt Agatha’s hand squeeze, but she didn’t pay attention. She said, “It’s Agatha’s.”

Rio didn’t realize what she’d done until she heard nothing but silence from the other end of the phone, coupled with Agatha’s nails digging into her arm. Her eyes snapped up to Agatha’s who had her lips pressed together. Her blue eyes were wide with distress and panic, and Rio opened her mouth, unsure of whether to take it back.

“Agatha lives in a brownstone,” James finally said. “Just like we do.”

Rio couldn’t help but glance around the apartment, one that was definitely not a brownstone. 

“I don’t know what to say,” was all Rio could blurt out. She didn’t know how to explain to James that Agatha didn’t live in a brownstone. She never had, as far as Rio was aware. She looked back at Agatha, eyebrows furrowed. What the hell was going on?

Wordlessly, Agatha held out her hand. After a moment of hesitation, Rio gave her the phone.

“Hello, James,” Agatha said. Her voice was remarkably even. Rio watched as the stress melted from her face, replaced by an eerie kind of focus. This must be what Agatha was like at work. “Yes, that is my apartment.” There was a pause before Agatha rolled her eyes. “Yes, I have two places, James. Is that really so hard to believe? Does it matter?” Then, James must have said something that made Agatha hesitate. Her eyes flickered over to Rio for a moment. “You’re paranoid.”

The call ended after that, and Agatha handed her the phone. The two of them stared at each other for a long moment before Agatha said, “You should go. James wants you home to talk about this.”

It felt wrong to just leave like this. Rio tried, “Agatha–”

“You need to talk to James.”

“But Agatha–”

“We did nothing wrong,” Agatha said, firm with an edge of warning. 

Nothing wrong recently, Rio wanted to say. A few months ago, they’d done plenty. Rio didn’t say this though. She could tell by the way Agatha held herself that she was not going to stand here and argue with her. 

Rio took a deep breath and said, “Fine. Good-bye, Agatha.”

Rio shoved her shoes back on and left without looking back. She knew she should have called a car, but she was still trembling from the panic and anger flooding her system. Rio just started walking. All she could do was focus on putting one foot in front of the other, so she could try to work off the excess emotions threatening to spill out. 

After about half an hour, Rio felt calm enough that she knew she wouldn’t snap the moment she tried to speak. She glanced around, assessing where she was, before she went to take the train the rest of the way home.

It was eerily quiet when Rio let herself in, but she expected that. She found James right where she expected him, sitting on the couch with a glass of whiskey in his hand. Rio stood at the end of the couch and stared. 

James took a long sip of his drink before he finally looked at her. “Why didn’t you tell me that you were spending so much time with Agatha?”

It came off as an accusation, and Rio tried to temper the flare of indignance that rose up in her. She took a deep breath and said, “I didn’t want to hurt you.” That was the truth. Maybe not the whole truth, but it wasn’t a lie. Rio’s hands clenched into tight fists. Rio continued, “You’re always trying so hard to get to know me, and I just can’t–”

“Rio, I get it,” James cut her off with a shake of his head. “You’re both women. It’s different.” He dragged a hand over his face and stood up, facing her. His shoulders were slumped, and his face was pale. He looked like hell. “It just hurts that you hid this from me. That you both hid this from me.” James stepped closer, allowing Rio to see the genuine hurt on his face. “Did you really think I’d disapprove of the two of you being friends?”

“No,” Rio said immediately. She hesitated and furrowed her brows. “I don’t know. I already saw how much it hurt you when you found out that I see Nicky. I didn’t want to make things worse.” Too late for that. “What if you and Agatha fought?”

James sighed and said, “It does hurt that you see Nicholas, but things aren’t exactly easy or simple between Agatha and me. I know that. I just–” He let out another sigh. He paced back and forth for a moment. When he stopped, he looked at her beseechingly. “I want you to tell me things, Rio. I’m your husband.”

“I know that,” Rio said.

James moved closer, frustration seeping into his voice. “I’m trying.”

“I know!” Rio exclaimed.

“Are you?” It would have been easier if James yelled at her, but instead, the question was asked in a broken voice, weak and confused.

Tears sprung to Rio’s eyes as she struggled to answer. Was she trying? She was, wasn’t she? Rio ended her affair with Agatha. She went on dates with James. She went to all of his events, family and work alike. Rio’s entire world revolved around the Harknesses now. Wasn’t that enough?

“I want this to work so much, Rio, but I can’t help but feel like you don’t,” James said. He finally reached out and touched her, a heavy hand on her shoulder. His brown eyes met hers, desperate. “I always feel like you’re just humoring me.”

Rio wrenched away from his touch and said, “What do you want me to say, James? You know I don’t love you. I never promised you I would either.”

“Can’t you try?” James all but begged.

“It doesn’t work like that!” Rio cried. She felt a few tears fall from her eyes and hastily wiped them away. She didn’t want him to see her cry. Rio took a shaky breath. She looked at him with teary eyes and said quietly, “Don’t you think I know how much easier things would be if I could just love you?”

Silence echoed in the moments following her words. The two of them could only stare at each other as the reality of their situation settled over them. James wanted things to be easy, to work. He wanted things to work like they were supposed to. A happily ever after. Meanwhile, Rio just wanted to survive. To tolerate her circumstances and find ways to make it easier. It was only a matter of time before James’s idealism shattered.

After several long moments, James sighed and dug the heels of his hands into his eyes. He rubbed at them tiredly before letting his hands fall back to his sides. “I’m sorry,” James said finally. “You’re right. It’s not fair of me to act like this when you didn’t promise me anything like that.”

Rio relaxed minutely. She didn’t expect him to apologize. Letting out a heavy sigh, Rio said, “For what it’s worth, I am sorry that I don’t love you.”

“Yet,” James said. It was a half-hearted attempt at humor, and the two of them shared small, exhausted smiles. “Come here.” He wrapped his arms around her into a hug, and while it was a kind, conciliatory gesture, Rio felt suffocated as she hugged him back. Thankfully, he kept the hug brief and pulled away after a few moments. He brushed a strand of hair from Rio’s face then said, “We still have to fix this thing with Agatha.”

“The photos?” Rio asked bitterly.

“Yes, we need to publicize our relationship with Agatha,” James said. Rio could see the way he shifted into politician mode, analyzing the right angle to play this. “We need to be seen together, coming from her apartment and spending time together. The last thing we need is some stupid tabloid trying to pit Agatha and myself against each other over you.”

Rio raised a brow. “Do you really think they’ll do that?”

“Harkness’s wife spends more time with his sister than himself. Is that marriage already on the rocks?” James replied, voice mocking the possible headlines. He shook his head, jaw clenched. He forced himself to take a deep breath. “Yes, I think that’s exactly what they’ll say.”

“Then we’ll fix it,” Rio said, because she hadn’t suffered this much to let this marriage fail like this. 

It was easy enough for James to call Agatha and explain the plan to her. A few outings together, beginning with a dinner tomorrow night. James already had the reservations. They would meet her there and put on an amicable show. Easy enough.

When James and Rio arrived at the restaurant the following night, Agatha was already there, and despite the reason they were there, Rio couldn’t help the way her breath caught at the sight of her.

Agatha looked ethereal in a light blue dress. It had a high neckline where the fabric layered on top of itself at the top before flowing all the way down to Agatha’s ankles. It was simple yet gorgeous. Agatha’s hair was also tied back for once in a low ponytail with a few strands framing her face. She looked soft like this. Harmless, Rio realized. A definitive non-threat.

“Agatha,” James greeted her first. “Lovely to see you.” The two of them hugged briefly, followed by Agatha kissing him lightly on the cheek. It was the first Rio had ever seen them do something like this, and she tried not to look too surprised when Agatha did the same to her. 

It was the first time Rio had felt her lips in months.

Agatha looked painfully unaware of how that simple kiss affected Rio, saying, “Shall we go in?”

The restaurant was upscale and bustling, full of plenty of other affluent and influential patrons. That was the point, Rio supposed. Make sure everyone who mattered saw them together. 

Once they were seated and food was ordered, Agatha asked, “How is work?”

“Work is work,” James replied lightly. “I would like your advice on something though.”

Rio tried to look interested as Agatha and James spoke about some congressman that needed to be swayed to James’s side for something. Although, from the sounds of it, it seemed more like blackmail than any kind of ethical persuasion. Rio didn’t say anything, merely watching Agatha light up at the idea of digging up dirt on this man.

Once the two of them figured out a way to presumably ruin this man’s life, James asked, “How is Nicholas?”

There was a moment of hesitation before Agatha recovered and said, “He’s doing well. We’re both nervous about the move, but we’re both looking forward to it as well.”

“It will be a big adjustment, I’m sure,” James nodded.

“We’ll figure things out,” Agatha said.

It was clear they never spoke about Nicky much. It also became much more clear why James was never invited to meet him. The exchange came off as so cold and perfunctory. It didn’t seem as though he actually cared. It felt as though he was just asking because he had to. 

Before the awkwardness could become too much, Rio asked, “Did he ask you about the record player?”

“What?” It was both Agatha and James who spoke, turning to her with twin looks of surprise.

Rio tried not to blush at both of their bewildered stares. She fidgeted with her fork. “Lilia is giving him the record player,” Rio explained. “He mentioned he was going to ask you if he can keep it in the living room or if he should keep it in his room.”

“It depends,” Agatha said.

“On?”

“What kind of music he has,” Agatha said, as if this was obvious.

Rio laughed and said, “Oh, and what music gets your stamp approval? Bach? Mozart?” Rio’s eyes lit up at another thought. “Oh, please tell me you’ll let him play Beyonce on his record player.”

“Is that how you see my music tastes?” Agatha snorted. “Classical music and Beyonce?”

Rio grinned and nodded, but as she did, she became aware of the fact that James was watching them. She tried to tamp down her nervousness as she looked at him. He didn’t look upset or angry. He just looked confused, most likely wondering where this camaraderie came from. Rio wasn’t sure she had an answer for him.

As the dinner continued, it was difficult. Rio wasn’t sure who to look at, who to speak to. She did her best to engage with them both equally, but she wasn’t sure she succeeded. It was just so much more comfortable with Agatha. That fact didn’t help the mounting tension between the three of them. For herself, Rio still felt awkward with James after their fight and with Agatha, feeling like she could act like she normally would with James there.

By the time they were finishing and heading back outside, Rio felt deeply unsettled.

Was this how it was going to be from now on? Putting on a show to make this loveless marriage seem flourishing? Rio wasn’t a stranger to wearing a mask and acting like everything was fine. All her life, she’d acted a certain way because that was how she was supposed to be. It just felt so cheap doing it for a marriage. Maybe Rio hated it so much because it kept her from Agatha.

Because that’s what it seemed to come to for Rio. Agatha. All she wanted was Agatha, her eyes, her laugh, her smile, her son. Rio wanted everything about her, but it was beginning to feel like she couldn’t have her even in that way, not even as friends, with the way things were going.

Could Rio handle losing Agatha altogether though, the one bright spot to all of this?

No, it was better to play along. 

So when the night was over and Agatha hugged her good-bye, Rio pressed her lips to Agatha’s cheek, just as she had done to her. This time, when Agatha pulled away, she had a look in her eye. Rio wasn’t quite sure what to call it. It was almost like she was hurt. 

That didn’t make any sense though, so Rio just smiled and said, “Good seeing, Agatha. We should do this again sometime.”

Agatha’s smile looked as fake as Rio’s felt as she said, “Of course, Rio. Just let me know when.”

Chapter End Notes

and we just spiral from here!!

it’s a lot of fun getting to write rio and james hit a breaking point where they’re both unhappy and unsatisfied and beginning to feel the effects of that so i hope you enjoyed :)

Chapter 16

Chapter Summary

Not that there was anything to move on from, Rio told herself. Not technically. Not officially. But actually…

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

After the photographs of Rio at Agatha’s apartment, there was a shift in Rio’s life.

Instead of dinners at Lilia’s and afternoons with Agatha, Rio found herself attending event after event with James. There were no more moments where Rio felt like she could breathe. There were only more dinners, more dates, more obligations. With every time that Rio forced herself into another dress to go to another occasion, she felt her misery and resentment grow. 

There had only been one other outing with Agatha and James, over a week ago, that was a lunch that was less than an hour.

Rio tried not to blame it on James, but it was hard not to. She knew what this marriage would consist of when she agreed to it, but after having months of freedom with Agatha, it felt confining and stifling to suddenly be forced back into this performative role.

Her only reprieve these days were when she went to volunteer at the hospital. Although she didn’t see Agatha there, Rio got to see Nicky at least. The boy was similar to his mother in the fact that he was someone who brightened her days.

“How’s living with Agatha?” Rio asked him one day over lunch.

“Good,” Nicky said. Before Rio could say anything, he hesitated then added, “Weird. I don’t know. It’s not bad.”

Rio chuckled and pushed her basket of fries towards him. “Go on,” Rio encouraged him. She had no idea if Nicky told his friends everything about Agatha, and it wasn’t like Nicky could talk to Agatha about this. 

Nicky lasted ten whole seconds before he blurted out, “It’s just so weird.”

“What’s weird about it?” Rio asked.

“Everything,” Nicky sighed. He picked up a fry and started ripping it apart. The action reminded Rio of when Agatha tore her brownie apart. That felt like years ago. “It’s hard because I don’t think either of us know how to act. Like, she’s my mom, but is she supposed to act like my mom now? Is she supposed to make me do chores or yell at me for staying up too late on a school night?”

“Well, I don’t think Agatha would ever yell at you,” Rio said absently. When Nicky gave her a look, Rio raised her hands in acquiesce and said, “Okay, sorry. Not helpful.” She thought about it for a moment and wondered who Agatha was talking to about this. She was sure Agatha probably felt as lost as Nicky did, but Rio hadn’t gotten more than a few texts from her recently. Rio shook her head. Focus on Nicky for now. 

“Why isn’t this easier?” Nicky huffed.

Rio reached out and squeezed his hand. She said, “The two of you have an unconventional relationship, so it’s going to be tough at first, but I know the two of you will figure it out. You’ll find something that works for you, and that’s all that matters.”

“But what if,” Nicky hesitated. “What if we fight?”

“Then you’ll really be mother and son,” Rio teased. She squeezed his hand again. “It’ll take some trial and error, but as long as you guys talk, it’ll work out.”

“I guess,” Nicky said reluctantly. He slumped back in his chair and pushed his pile of mushed potato away. He fiddled with his napkin before he looked at Rio and asked, “Will you come over soon? We haven’t had dinner in a while.”

Rio had gone to one last dinner with Lilia before she moved away, but she hadn’t been to a dinner with Nicky since.

“I’ll try,” Rio said, not wanting to disappoint him if she couldn’t. “I’ve been busy lately.”

“With James.” It wasn’t a question.

Rio shifted uneasily. “Yeah, with James.”

Nicky looked out at the crowd in the cafeteria. After a moment, he said, “She doesn’t talk about him a lot. I don’t think she likes him.”

Rio let out a heavy sigh. “It’s complicated,” Rio said, which in all honestly was putting it lightly. 

“Actually complicated or you just don’t want to talk about it complicated?” Nicky asked.

“Both.”

The two of them shared wry smiles. As Rio cleaned up their trays, Nicky leaned forward and said, “Well, just so you know, I miss you. Both of us do.”

Rio’s hands froze where they were picking up a few napkins. She swallowed as she slowly lowered the napkins onto her tray. She wished those words didn’t affect her so much, but they did because Rio missed them too. If only she could hear Agatha say that too.

Forcing a smile, Rio said, “Thanks, Nicky. I’ll try and visit soon.”

Nicky’s words weighed heavily on Rio for the rest of the day, reminding her of the exhaustion that seemed to be a permanent fixture in her life lately. That was why when James told her the following afternoon that there was an auction they needed to attend that night, Rio said, “No.”

James looked up from his phone and stared at her. “No?” James repeated, not quite angry. More baffled. “What do you mean no?”

“I mean, no,” Rio said slowly. She stood up from the couch and wrapped her arms around herself. “I know I’m your wife, James, and I know those pictures looked bad, but it’s been weeks. I’m exhausted. I don’t want to go tonight.”

“Rio,” James began. He stopped himself and sighed. He walked closer and stopped just a few feet away from her. “I know I’ve been asking a lot of you lately, but it’s necessary.”

Wasn’t it always?

“I know, but I’m telling you right now,” Rio said. “My going with you tonight is not necessary.”

James stared at her for a long moment before saying, “Fine.” Judging by his tone though, it clearly wasn’t fine. James shoved his hands into his pockets and said, “This isn’t me asking you to love me.”

“I know.”

“This was the agreement.”

“I know,” Rio repeated, annoyed. “But I’m tired, James. One night isn’t going to end our marriage.”

James sighed and shook his head. He said nothing else, which was fine with Rio. She silently watched him get ready and leave without another word. As soon as the door shut behind him, Rio let herself breathe. She rubbed her eyes and tried not to feel too overwhelmed. She hadn’t realized just how much she relied on Agatha to keep her sane.

With nothing to do, Rio lazed about on the couch before she made herself a cup of instant ramen for dinner. It was as she was eating that she scrolled through her phone, apprising herself of the news.

The last thing Rio expected to see was an article on Agatha.

The headline read, “Senator Harkness’s Sister Flaunting Secret Lovechild and Lesbian Lover.” Accompanying the article was a photograph of Agatha walking out of her apartment, not her brownstone, with Nicky and another woman. Nicky was wearing his backpack, most likely going to school, but it was the woman that had all of Rio’s attention. She was gorgeous with long red hair. She was wearing a suit like Agatha, and Rio couldn’t help but think they’d make an attractive couple.

As soon as the thought entered her brain, Rio leapt off the couch and shoved her shoes on. She barely remembered to grab her wallet before she left the apartment. She didn’t even bother with a car, heading straight for the train.

The entire ride there, Rio felt herself brimming with fury and betrayal. Weeks. Weeks, Rio hadn’t heard from Agatha. It wasn’t for lack of trying either. Rio texted Agatha every so often, but her attempts were always met with curt messages that made it clear that she wasn’t wanted. Now, there was this. Rio had to find out from a tabloid that Nicky was revealed to the world and Agatha was dating someone. 

Had Agatha really moved on that quickly?

Not that there was anything to move on from, Rio told herself. Not technically. Not officially. But actually…

Rio clenched her jaw so tightly it ached, but it was either that or let out a scream that would definitely get her institutionalized. By the time Rio got off the train, she was shaking with restrained rage. 

It was proof of how furious she was that Rio didn’t even stop to consider that Nicky would be home until he opened the door. The two of them stared at each other in silent surprise until Nicky finally said, “Hey. I didn’t know you were coming over.”

“Unplanned,” Rio managed to say, but even she could hear how strained her voice was. “I need to talk to Agatha.”

Nicky eyed her for a moment before he nodded. “Mom, I’m going for a walk!” Nicky called out.

Mom. That was new. Just another thing Rio didn’t know about. 

There was a shuffle of footsteps before Agatha came into view, reading something on her phone, saying, “A walk? Why are you–” Her words came to an abrupt end when she looked up and saw Rio standing there. 

“I’ll be back in an hour,” Nicky said. He glanced between the two of them. “Maybe two.”

Agatha’s gaze snapped back to him. “Nicky–”

“I have my phone,” Nicky said. “I’ll stay in the area. I’ll be fine.”

Agatha twisted her lips into a frown. She walked over to her purse and fished out a twenty dollar bill. She held it out and said, “Sit in a cafe instead. Do your reading for school.”

“Thanks,” Nicky said. He grabbed the money and his backpack from the floor. He gave Rio a playful salute before he brushed past her, whispering, “Good luck.”

Rio’s odds seemed dismally poor if a teenager was wishing her luck. She watched him walk down the hall, and it wasn’t until he turned the corner that she looked back at Agatha. If Nicky had looked surprised yet happy to see Rio, Agatha only looked displeased. 

“Since you’re already here, you might as well come in,” Agatha said.

Rio took a deep breath and stepped instead, closing and locking the door behind her. She followed Agatha into the living room. She tried to ignore the way that an apartment that once felt like a second home now felt like such an unwelcome space. 

Agatha didn’t even offer Rio a drink. She merely spun on her heel and demanded, “What do you want?”

Too much to say. Rio settled for, “I saw the article about Nicky.”

“And that requires a house call?” Agatha said snidely. 

Rio bit her lip and tried not to lash out. “Agatha,” she said, “I just wanted to check on you. We haven’t spoken in weeks.”

Agatha eyed her for a moment before she shrugged, tossing her hair over her shoulder. “I thought I was doing you a favor,” Agatha said simply. “I mean, you were clearly busy with James. Why bother you?”

“You aren’t a bother,” Rio snapped. She felt tears prick her eyes and forced herself to take a deep breath. When she calmed herself, she found Agatha staring at her with sharp eyes. Rio didn’t flinch. Instead, she said, “Is that why you didn’t tell me about her?” It was only then that Rio hesitated. “That woman in the photo–”

Agatha cut her off swiftly and firmly, “What about her?”

Rio licked her lips and tried to read Agatha’s expression. All she could tell was that she seemed annoyed. That wasn’t exactly helpful. Rio asked as evenly as she could, “Who is she?”

“I don’t see how it’s any of your business,” Agatha said, and it was the way she said, like Rio was nobody, that made her break.

“Was it all just a lie?” Rio asked. It came out more as a cry, but she couldn’t help it now. “Us? Nicky?” A family, one that Rio tricked herself into believing was real. Rio’s nails dug into her palm as she stared at Agatha. Her voice cracked as she said, “Why would you let me in if you were just going to cast me aside the moment you found someone else?”

Agatha held no sympathy for her though. She scoffed, “Oh, so you’re the only one to have a life? Don’t forget your the one who goes home to a husband every night.” The blow struck Rio ruthlessly. A slap to the face would have hurt less. She barely pulled herself together in time to see the victorious smirk flicker across Agatha’s face. “What does it matter, Rio? Why do you care?” Agatha asked, walking closer. “Shouldn’t you be happy for me as a friend?”

“Stop it,” Rio said.

“No, tell me,” Agatha insisted. She was close now, just inches from Rio. She leaned into her space, crowding her, making her look at her. “Tell me why it’s so hard for you to know that there actually might be someone else in my life.”

“Agatha, stop it,” Rio pleaded.

Agatha wouldn’t stop though. “Does it drive you crazy? Thinking about how I could leave you and go home to another woman who I–”

The words that threatened to pour out of her were too frightening for Rio to even conceive, and instead, she grabbed Agatha by the shirt and crashed her lips into hers. It was a messy, harsh kiss, one born of desperation and fear, but Rio meant it nonetheless. Craved it, even. As painful as the kiss was, it was the first time Rio had kissed Agatha in months, and the touch made a part of her crumble.

Agatha kissed her back for the briefest of moments before she roughly shoved Rio away.

“No,” Agatha said. Her blue eyes were alight with rage. “You don’t get to do this.” She pressed a finger hard against Rio’s chest, right over her heart. “You either want me, or you don’t. You don’t get to pick and choose when you want to fuck.”

Rio wanted to tell her it was more than that. Agatha had to know that, didn’t she? It was never about the sex. It was only ever about Agatha. All Rio needed was Agatha. 

“Agatha, please,” Rio tried. The tears that had been threatening to spill this entire time finally fell, streaming down Rio’s cheeks.

“Please what?” Agatha said. She gripped Rio’s shirt tight for a moment before she pushed her away. “I’m fucking sick of this, Rio. I’ve let you treat me like your little play thing for too long. First, you want me. Then, you don’t. Then, you do but only as a friend. Then, you fucking look at me sometimes like–” Agatha stopped herself, and Rio desperately wished she’d kept going. Agatha shook her head and continued, “I can’t do this anymore. I won’t.”

Rio knew what she had to say. She just had to open her mouth and say it. But when she tried, nothing came out. The tears kept coming. Rio couldn’t do it. She was paralyzed by fear, but she couldn’t even say fear of what. Rejection? Betrayal? Change?

Say it. Just say it. Tell her you love her. 

The word love made Rio choke, the sheer terror of loving a woman who could make her entire world shatter. Would that be so bad though? She’d already turned it on its head. 

I love you. That was all Rio had to say. 

When was the last time Rio had ever told someone that? 

Rio couldn’t remember. 

Finally, Agatha sighed and looked away. “Just go,” Agatha said quietly. 

And all Rio could do was go. 

Go, go, go. She kept going until she found herself back in her apartment, and as soon as she was, Rio collapsed to her knees. The tears flowed freely now as ragged sobs were finally let loose. Rio wrapped her arms around herself as the crushing realization of what she lost hit her full force. 

What had she done? What had her cowardice cost her? 

Agatha was never going to forgive her for this. She was gone, for good this time. 

Rio cried harder, clawing at her chest like she might be able to rip her heart out and stop the pain that threatened to swallow her whole. She couldn’t though. All she could do was cry, and that was what she did until a pair of arms guided her to bed. 

For a moment, she let herself actually believe it might be Agatha, but as she laid down, all she saw were James’s brown eyes.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 17

Chapter Summary

The first few days after Rio’s confrontation with Agatha found her a shell of a person. 

Chapter Notes

thank you so much for all the comments on the last chapter (even if most of them were upset with me) and thank you for sticking it out with this fic :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The first few days after Rio’s confrontation with Agatha found her a shell of a person. 

Rio barely left the bed, barely ate any food, barely slept despite her best efforts. Her chest just felt so hollow, like someone had carved out her heart and left her to bleed. No matter her attempts to staunch the loss, Rio still felt empty and astray, missing something she can’t recover.

She was mourning, for all intents and purposes. She was grieving the loss of the woman she loved. Rio couldn’t tell James that though. She actually didn’t tell him anything. All he knew was that she was devastated for reasons that she refused to say.

Eventually, when Rio finally collected the shattered pieces of herself and forced them back together into some crude semblance of a functioning human being, it was right back to how things were before.

Rio was James’s wife, always on his arm at every event.

That was all she was now. 

When did that happen? When had Rio’s very being become so inextricably tied to the Harknesses, both of them?

For the first time since they got married, Rio didn’t go to the monthly family dinner. She couldn’t stomach the thought of seeing Agatha, let alone sitting through an entire dinner with her. Rio made up some weak excuse about not feeling well, and even though she knew James didn’t believe it for a moment, he let her stay home.

“Are you ever going to trust me enough to talk to me?” James asked. 

“It’s not about trust.”

James huffed a laugh and looked at her. “Then what is it, Rio? I keep doing everything I’m supposed to and yet…”

“Not yet,” Rio said, to which James could only sigh. 

Maybe she would tell him when the thought of Agatha no longer made her want to cry or when she was brave enough to admit what, who, she wanted. Or maybe, she’d keep it locked inside herself for the rest of her life.

Life went on though, and it took almost three weeks for Rio to work up the nerve to go back to the hospital for volunteer work. It felt ridiculous, helping others when she couldn’t even help herself, but it gave herself something to do instead of staring at a wall and replaying her last conversation with Agatha again and again in her head. 

Once she returned, it didn’t take long for Nicky to find her. If Rio didn’t know any better, she would have thought he was staking out her usual spots. When he did run into her, right as she was about to leave, Nicky latched onto her sleeve with wide eyes.

“Rio!” Nicky exclaimed. He threw his arms around her in a clumsy hug. They’d never hugged before. Rio hugged him back though, trying to ignore the way it made her heart thud a little harder. It hurt. “What happened? Where have you been?”

“I–” Rio couldn’t think of an excuse.

Nicky’s eyebrows scrunched together as he stared at her. His arms dropped back to his sides. Nicky’s lips curved into a frown, so much like Agatha’s, before he asked, “What happened between you and Mom? She was crying when I came home, and she refuses to talk about it.”

It should have made her feel better, knowing Agatha was hurt too, but it only made Rio feel worse. Rio shook her head slowly and said, “It’s between us, Nicky.”

“But it’s not fair,” Nicky said. His wide brown eyes looked at her in betrayal. “You were there, and suddenly, you’re not. Everything’s changed, but you were supposed to stick with us.”

Rio wasn’t sure if it was something genetic or learned, but Agatha and Nicky both had the uncanny ability to say things that made Rio feel as though she’d been stabbed. Repeatedly. She had no idea Nicky felt that way about her. She knew Nicky didn’t have a lot of adults in his life he could talk to, but she didn’t expect her absence to affect him so deeply.

“I’m sorry,” was all Rio could say. She reached out and laid her hand on Nicky’s shoulder, relieved when he didn’t move away. She squeezed it and tried to sound as sincere as possible. “I am really sorry I made you feel that, Nicky. I didn’t mean to just disappear on you.” She let go and gave a wobbly smile. “Things just have been really rough lately, and I don’t think Agatha wants me around anyways.”

Nicky stared at her for a long time before he whispered, “What happened between you two?”

Too much and not enough. “I’m going to leave it up to Agatha to decide what you know,” Rio said. “She’s your mom.”

“Fine,” Nicky sighed. His shoulders curled in on himself as he shuffled his feet. He peered at her and asked, “But you’re back at the hospital now? You were gone for a while.”

“Yeah, I’m back,” Rio said.

Nicky gave a sharp nod. He bit his lip. Rio waited. Finally, he said, “Maybe you can help me with my math and biology homework sometime. Mom’s really bad at it.”

Ignoring the way the mention of Agatha made her ache, Rio smiled and said, “I’d love to.”

The two of them talked about what Nicky was learning in school for a moment before Rio finally excused herself to leave. Instead of heading straight home like she planned, she made the detour to go to Pancho’s. 

As soon as she walked in, Carol said, “I am not taking you home again.”

Rio blushed and took a seat at the bar, saying, “I promise I’m just here for one drink.” She fidgeted with her fingers for a moment before she added, “Thanks, by the way. For that night.”

“No problem,” Carol shrugged. She poured Rio some whiskey and slid it over. “Things any better now?”

“Worse,” Rio sighed.

Carol winced. She playfully pretended to try to take the whiskey away, but Rio laughed and held it out of reach. Carol chuckled and leaned against the back counter. She asked, “Want to talk about it?”

“Not this time,” Rio said with a shake of her head. 

Carol eyed her for a moment then nodded. “Alright, well, let me know if you need anything.”

Left alone, Rio held glass between her hands and stared at the amber liquid. As she always did lately, when left alone with her thoughts, Rio thought about Agatha. She couldn’t get her words out of her head. 

I’ve let you treat me like your little play thing for too long… I can’t do this anymore.

Rio knew she messed up. It was just hard to figure out exactly when this mess really began. Was it her wedding night, when she was with Agatha for the first time? Or, was it even before that, when Rio agreed to this marriage at all? 

The when didn’t really matter though. It just mattered that Rio had, in fact, messed up. She messed up with James, but more importantly to her, she messed up with Agatha. It had never been her intention to play with Agatha’s feelings, but looking back on the last few months, Rio knew that’s exactly what she’d done with her back-and-forth, her desire to have it all instead of just choosing. 

It was impossible to deny this when Rio thought of Agatha’s expression that night. Angry, yes, but also undeniably hurt. Did it hurt because Agatha felt the same way? Rio tried not to dwell on the possibility, but she couldn’t help but wonder. It was stupid of her though. What did it matter if she felt the same way if Rio was still stuck in the same place, unable to do anything about it?

Rio needed something to change, but she wasn’t sure what she could actually change. Or rather, what she was willing to change. Was she really ready to give up on this marriage, to come out of the closest, and to lose her family forever? The first two didn’t sound so bad, but the last made her chest feel so tight. 

Even after all of this, Rio couldn’t let go of her family. They were her family. What was a family without sacrifice?

Rubbing her temple, Rio could feel herself already beginning to spiral at the thought of her family. She needed someone to talk to, and there was only one person she knew who would understand.

It’d been months since she last saw Alice due to their schedules, but maybe it was time to finally catch up. All it took was a text, one that Alice responded to promptly and excitedly, and they were set to have a last-minute dinner at Alice’s tonight. The ease with which it happened made Rio feel guilty all over again. With everything that had been going on with Agatha and James, she hadn’t been a very good friend to Alice recently.

It was just one mistake after another, it seemed. 

Although she stayed true to her word and only had one drink, Rio lingered at the bar until it was time for her to go to Alice’s. It was easier to sulk there than it was in the apartment. 

When Rio made it to Alice’s place, her best friend threw open the door and exclaimed, “Rio!” Alice hugged Rio tightly, and it took everything in Rio not to burst into tears right then in there. Even though she managed not to, Alice could still tell something was wrong when she pulled back. She didn’t say anything though. She just smiled and said, “I got us pizza and wine.”

The two of them made themselves comfortable on the couch, and Rio let Alice tell her all about what she’d been up to lately. It sounded like her friend was doing well. Work was okay, maybe even a promotion soon. She’d picked up the piano again; she was even thinking about buying one. There was even a woman she was seeing, someone sharp yet kind, that made Alice smile dopily. 

“What about you?” Alice asked with a knowing look. She poured Rio another glass of wine.

Rio didn’t answer at first, trying to find the words. “I, uh,” Rio tried, and to her embarrassment, she felt her throat close up. “Alice, I,” she tried again, and this time, her voice cracked. She shook her head and accepted the fact that there was no being brave or strong when talking about this. “Alice, I really fucked up this time,” Rio told her tearfully.

Alice reached out and held her hand. Her face was nothing but quiet understanding as she said, “Hey, whatever happened, you can talk to me.”

So, Rio finally talked to her about it. All of it. From the first dinner where she initially thought she hated Agatha, even as she was simultaneously attracted to her, to the affair, to their friendship, to its devastating end. Rio told her everything, even as she cried through all of it. 

What hurt the most, she realized, was talking about the last month of it or so. It was then that Rio had felt the most at peace, the most at home, the most loved. She felt like she’d finally found a family after being used by her own, but by her own selfishness, she’d lost them. The irony wasn’t lost on her either. Rio was selfless enough to put herself into this mess for her family, but she was too selfish to go through the pain of getting herself out. Instead, she hurt Agatha and Nicky, and that was what hurt most of all. 

“I’m sorry you’ve been struggling with this alone,” Alice said. She had her arms around Rio now, hugging her close. “I’m not mad, I swear, but why didn’t you tell me about this sooner? You and Agatha?”

“I was scared,” Rio said. She sniffled and accepted the tissue Alice handed her. “Even if I don’t love him, I still cheated, Alice, and that’s–” Rio sighed. “That doesn’t make it okay.”

“Rio, if this friendship hinged on the fact that we never did anything wrong, this friendship would have ended back in college,” Alice replied.

Rio couldn’t help but crack a smile. “The great cheating crisis of 2007,” she said solemnly.

“You were so mad,” Alice recalled with a laugh. “I really thought you were never going to talk to me again after I told you about that test.”

“I’m glad I didn’t do that,” Rio said.

Alice gave her a gentle smile and hugged her tight again. She stayed like that until her arms were tired. When she pulled back, Alice asked, “So, what next? What do you want, Rio?”

“I don’t know.”

“Liar,” Alice said without missing a beat.

Rio exhaled slowly and fought the urge to snap. Her voice was still angry, but it wasn’t rude as she said, “Fine. I want Agatha. And Nicky. I want things to go back to the way they were before.”

“No, you don’t,” Alice said, shaking her head. “We all know that was never going to work out. Not the way you wanted it to.” She poked Rio’s forehead and said, “You’re not happy, and don’t give me that bullshit about how no one is happy. You’re miserable, Rio, and I don’t want you to lose yourself over this.”

“Too late for that,” Rio mumbled.

“Shut up,” Alice sighed. “You are still the brilliant and kind and thoughtful person you were a year ago. You’ve just… hit a few bumps in the road.”

Rio said dryly, “More like I drove full speed over them and careened out of control.”

“I was trying to be gentle,” Alice said, but she was smiling gently. “This doesn't have to be the end, if you don’t want it to be. This life with James, this doesn’t have to be yours for the rest of your days.”

“You make it sound so easy,” Rio groaned. She slumped back against the couch and dragged her hands over her face. “Imagine my parents’ reaction if I told them I was divorcing him. No, wait, I’m not just divorcing him, but I’m divorcing him because I’m gay.” Rio let her hands fall back into her lap and sighed. She grasped her wedding ring between her fingers, twisting it back and forth, as she said, voice small, “They’d be so disappointed in me.”  

Alice held her hand, but she didn’t say anything. Not at first. She seemed just as deep in thought as Rio. Eventually though, Alice said, “I think a lot about what my mom would’ve wanted for me. It’s hard to really know though. I don’t think I really knew her when I was younger, not the real her.” Alice took a deep breath and shook her head. “I try to think about what I do remember though. I know she loved music and dancing. I know she loved eating cold leftovers and hot coffee. Maybe I only want to remember the good stuff because she died, but I also like to think she loved seeing me happy.”

“That’s not fair,” Rio argued quietly. “Your mom died in some freak accident at work because she was trying to save money for your college, Alice. Of course she wanted you to be happy. My parents chose to go into politics and marry me off to someone who’d help my dad’s connections. One is clearly more about the child.”

The jab was unfair, but Alice merely replied, “For all we know, my mom wanted me to go to college to become an accountant.”

Rio snorted, “Right, your hippie mom would have loved that.”

“Listen, my point is that I get it,” Alice said. She squeezed Rio’s hand and turned to face her. “Only daughter wants to do right by her parents because of everything they did for her and all the cultural implications that go along with that for us. Trust me when I say my therapist has had to beat that mentality out of me with a thousand hammers.” Rio smiled slightly, and Alice smiled back, earnest and sympathetic. 

“And don’t get me wrong,” Alice continued. “I still think about doing my best to honor my mom every goddamn day, but I’ve realized I’m not going to do that by doing some bullshit that would make me miserable. I do right by my mom by living my life as best as I can by helping others and being happy. Because that’s all a parent should want at the end of the day. For their child to be happy.”

The petulant part of Rio wanted to say it was different. Her parents were not like Lorna Wu. She held herself back though, mulling over Alice’s words. It sounded so obvious when she put it like that, but Rio also couldn’t help but feel like that wasn’t true for herself. If her parents really wanted her to be happy, wouldn’t they have let her marry someone else? Did they just not think she’d care if she married James? 

Rio swallowed, throat feeling tight once more. Or, was it that they knew she wouldn’t be happy but convinced her to do it anyway? And if that was true, if her parents were not like Lorna Wu, did that mean they truly loved her at all? If Rio divorced James and ruined their plans, would they forgive her? And if they didn’t, did that mean they were in the wrong, not Rio?

A thousand questions swam through Rio’s mind, and Rio couldn’t even begin to fathom answering a fraction of them.

Alice seemed to sense this though. She squeezed her hand again. “Just think about it,” Alice told her. 

Rio nodded, but she knew that this was not something so easily considered. She needed space to figure all of this out for herself. This wasn’t something she could think about around James or even in their shared apartment.

The perfect excuse to get away came in the form of an invitation two days later. Her Aunt Carla was turning sixty. She was having a big party to celebrate, and she wanted everyone in the family to come for the following weekend. Conveniently, Aunt Carla lived all the way in Texas. 

Surrounded by the family she hadn’t seen in years wasn’t the ideal situation to think about possibly divorcing her husband, but it would have to do.

Rio called her aunt to let her know she was coming and booked her flight to Texas that same night.

In the end, something had to give.

Chapter 18

Chapter Summary

Even hundreds of miles away, Agatha seemed to invade Rio’s thoughts. 

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Despite Rio’s insistence it was unnecessary, James drove her to the airport. 

The car ride was silent. James didn’t even bother turning on the radio. Rio stared out the window, watching the scenery pass by, pretending that things weren’t so bad between them. They were though. Things had only gotten worse between them.

It was hard to believe just a month or two ago that Rio and James lived happily together. They would eat meals together, and they would talk to each other. They would watch a movie every so often, and they would joke under their breaths at the events they attended. Whatever semblance of comfort and ease between them had been washed away with the photographs of Rio and the ensuing fallout. 

These days, the two of them rarely spoke. When they did, it was usually when they were out together, putting on a show that hid away that fractured nature of their relationship. If they happened to try to talk to each other at home, it was awkward and stilted. The tension only ever seemed to grow, even when they tried their best to try to make things better. All they could feel was the mounting frustration at their relationship, one that couldn’t seem to work. 

There was no going back for them, it seemed. 

Rio missed James more than she thought she would. He was her friend, despite it all, but now, she wondered if she was more like his enemy. 

As he parked at the passenger drop-off, James stared straight ahead as he said, “Have a safe flight. Text me when you land.”

Rio hesitated with her hand on the door handle. She glanced at James and sighed. “I know this isn’t the best time, but we need to talk,” she said. She needed to get this off her chest before she left. “We’re both clearly unhappy, but we’ve never really had a real conversation about why or how to fix that. So we should do that. Talk. Instead of brooding like a couple of angsty teenagers.”

James huffed quietly, a small laugh. Slowly, he turned to look at her. He studied her face for a moment before he managed a small smile. “You’re right,” James said. He reached out and laid his hand on her shoulder. He squeezed it and suggested tentatively, “We can talk when you get back?”

“Sounds good,” Rio said, smiling back. 

Since her parents flew the day before, on Friday, Rio was alone for her flight. She didn’t mind though. Traveling with her parents was stressful, and being alone gave her the chance to do some reading. 

Once she was settled in her seat on the plane, Rio ended up dozing off for the first half, but after she woke up, she grabbed her book from her backpack. It had been a while since she got to read for pleasure, but Rio was excited. The book she picked up, Cantoras , was set during the Uruguayan dictatorship and focused on a group of queer women finding each other during such a tumultuous time. 

Rio flipped open to the first page, and in an instant, she was pulled into the world of the book, following the characters as they found their safe haven together. It made the rest of her flight go by quickly, almost too quickly, and Rio had to blink hard to reorient herself when the announcement came out that they would be landing soon.

After tucking her book away, Rio took a deep breath and mentally braced herself for the coming weekend. It was really only this evening and half of tomorrow, but she already knew it would be more than enough.

Rio couldn’t remember the last time the whole family on her dad’s side came together. It must have been when Rio graduated medical school, almost four years ago. So much had happened since then, including one of her cousins having a child, and while the family was fairly good about texting about the big moments, it still wasn’t the same as seeing everyone in person.

Because her aunt, along with her grandparents, lived on a large plot of land far from the city, it took Rio over an hour to get there. When she finally arrived, the last thing she wanted was to be bombarded by family, but that was just how things went. Plus, Rio had missed them.

Using her spare key, Rio let herself into the house. She barely shut the door behind her before a tiny body launched itself at her. Rio dropped her duffel bag in order to catch Sofia, eight years-old and so tall already, in her arms. She hugged the little girl tightly and exclaimed, “Look at you! You didn’t look this big over FaceTime.”

“I’m gonna be taller than you, Tía Rio,” Sofia told her with a wide, toothy grin. “Next time you see me, I’m gonna be eight feet tall.”

“Eight feet?” Rio laughed. “What are your parents feeding you?”

“Lots of vegetables.”

Rio looked up as her oldest cousin joined them. Victor looked as he always did, broad shoulders with a carefully trimmed beard and cropped curls. Despite it just being a family get together, he still wore slacks and a button-up, something their other cousins undoubtedly already teased him for. Rio set Sofia down to hug him.

“¿Estás bien?” Victor asked her. “We don’t hear much from you these days.”

“I’m fine,” Rio said. “Just busy.”

Sofia tugged on Rio’s arm and said, “You’re supposed to say, ‘estoy bien’, Tía Rio.”

Rio laughed while Victor explained, “We’ve been trying to teach Sofia more Spanish. Don’t want her to be like you or Gabriel.”

“I can speak Spanish,” Rio said defensively.

“And yet I never hear you speaking it unless it’s to our abuela,” Victor replied with a raised brow.

Rio bit the inside of her cheek but said nothing else. She left her bag by the door and let Sofia pull her to the living room, where the rest of the family was. Victor’s wife sat on the couch with Gabriel and Miguel, brothers and Rio’s other cousins, while Rio’s grandmother sat on the other couch. In the kitchen, Rio could hear her parents with her aunts and uncles, probably finishing up with dinner. 

“Look who’s finally here!” Miguel cheered, standing up. The same age as Rio, he was always her closest confidante at these things. It helped that he was so outgoing too, the perfect balance to Rio’s more quiet demeanor. 

Rio accepted Miguel’s hug with ease and said, “It’s good to see you.” She looked around and teased, “Still no girlfriend, I see. I bet your parents love that.” Miguel was blessed with his mother’s dark curls and his father’s green eyes, and from the moment he became aware of the fact that girls did in fact exist, he’d been wreaking havoc in the world of love.

Gabriel joined them, hugging Rio too. He was Miguel’s older brother, and when Victor wasn’t around, he took it upon himself to watch over them. His wife wasn’t here, but that wasn’t strange. His wife had no strong fondness for their family. “I was just talking to him about that,” Gabriel said. “Don’t you think it’s time for him to settle down?”

“Already?” Miguel gasped. He slung an arm around Rio and said, “We’re just hitting our prime, aren’t we?”

“Rio’s married,” Gabriel reminded him.

Miguel exaggeratedly looked around. “I don’t see a husband. Do you?” He grinned down at Rio and teased, “Where’s that gringo? Maybe if he came, Sarah would have come too.”

“Sarah had work,” Gabriel sighed, excusing his wife’s absence.

“Right, work,” Miguel drawled. “Just like she’s had work during every other family gathering. Nothing to do with the fact that she still can’t eat our food.”

“Bennett is sick too, so either way, she wouldn’t have been able to come,” Gabriel added with a glare.

Miguel pouted and pressed a hand to his chest. “Our poor Benito. How will he ever get better without mamá’s special soup?”

Gabriel’s face reddened, but Rio cut in before they could get into a fight already. “James is working,” Rio said. “So I guess I’ll be right there with Gabriel from now on.”

“Aw, but it’s not nearly as fun giving you shit,” Miguel grinned. He ruffled her hair and said, “Come on. You look like you could use a drink.”

“Let me say hi to my parents first,” Rio said. 

Miguel gave her a salute and said, “And that’s why they always brag about you. Always with the manners and respect.”

He meant it teasingly, but Rio felt her smile grow strained anyway. She patted his back and slipped away to the kitchen. She greeted her aunts and uncles, pressing kisses to their cheeks as she went, until she found her parents by the pantry.

Luis noticed her first, shouting joyfully, “Rio!” He swept her into a tight hug and pressed a kiss to her forehead. “It’s been too long.” He pinched her cheek and said, “Tell your husband to give me less work, so I can see you more.”

Rio laughed uncomfortably, but Luis didn’t notice. He passed her off to Paola, who hugged her just as tight, tutting, “Have you lost weight? You’re so skinny.”

Although she heard such comments all her life, Paola was actually right this time. Rio had lost several pounds thanks to the stress of the last few months. Rio just smiled though and said, “I’ve just missed your cooking. I’ll make sure to load up while I’m here.”

“I can give you the recipes,” Paola told her.

“You always tell me it’s from YouTube,” Rio reminded her. “Or, you just make it up as you go, so you can’t actually tell me what’s in it.”

“Trust your tongue,” Paola said, wagging her finger at her.

Rio laughed, “My tongue isn’t as well trained as yours.”

“Then train it!” Paola said. “How else will you cook for James?”

Rio rolled her eyes. With her filial greeting done, she slipped back out to the living room. “And there’s my favorite person!” Rio exclaimed dramatically. “Saved the best for last.” Her smile was wide as she sat down next to her grandmother, Claudia, looping her arm through hers. “Cómo estás?”

“ Mejor ahora que estás aquí,” Claudia said. Better now that you’re here. She patted Rio’s cheek and asked, “ Dónde estás tu esposo?” Where’s your husband?”

Rio refrained from making a face at the immediate question about James. “Esta trabajando,” Rio said. He’s working.

“Él debería estar aquí,” Claudia said in clear disapproval. He should be here. “Qué es más importante que tu familia?” What’s more important than your family?

And wasn’t that the question? Rio leaned into her grandmother and said placatingly, “La proxima vez.” Next time.

Claudia eyed Rio before she pinched the skin between her thumb and forefinger. Rio yelped and yanked her hand away. She rubbed it with a glare, but her grandmother stared at her, unrepentant. “¿Y tu familia? ¿Cuando me vas a dar otro bisnieto?” And what about your family? When are you going to give me another great-grandchild?

“No sé,” Rio shrugged. I don’t know. 

“No sé,” Claudia scoffed. “¡Deberías estar diciendo pronto! ¡Lo más rápido posible!”  You should be saying soon! As soon as possible!

Rio nodded obligingly, but she was relieved when it was announced that dinner was finally ready. She helped Claudia to the table before she took her seat towards the other end of the table. She ended up between Sofia and Paola, with Miguel across from her. Initially, Rio was worried her mother would spend the entire dinner asking her about James, but to her relief, Sofia took up most of her attention.

From the moment she was born, Rio adored Sofia, finally another girl in their family. Rio spoiled her as best as she could, FaceTiming her more often than she did any other family member. Talking to her now, Sofia reminded her of Nicky in a lot of ways, shy and thoughtful. It made her wonder what Nicky was like when he was younger.

Was he just as shy? Was he even shyer than he was now? What would it have been like watching him grow up, the way she had with Sofia?

Rio wondered how often Agatha had these same kinds of thoughts.

The reminder of Agatha struck Rio suddenly. She felt her grip tighten around her fork as she forced herself to keep her breathing even. 

Even hundreds of miles away, Agatha seemed to invade Rio’s thoughts. 

Once again, Rio became aware of the dull ache that had never faded. It would always be there, as far as Rio was concerned, for as long as Rio didn’t have Agatha in her life. The melodramatics of the thought made her want to laugh, but deep down, Rio knew it was true. It just became more and more apparent to her the longer Rio thought about everything that had happened.

Agatha was her one true taste of freedom, her one safe space where Rio didn’t have to be anyone but herself. Not the perfect daughter. Not the perfect wife. Just Rio, imperfections and all. 

And Rio didn’t want to lose that. She didn’t want to lose Agatha. 

What an insane revelation to have at her family dinner.

“Tía Rio, are you okay?”

Rio startled so badly that she dropped her fork, sending it clattering to the floor. She blushed as everyone’s eyes went to her. She cleared her throat and said, “Sorry, I spaced out for a second.”

“Always with your head in the clouds,” Carla tutted.

Rio didn’t breathe again until everyone went back to their conversations. She smiled down at Sofia, who still stared at her with concern. “I’m okay,” Rio assured her. “I was just thinking.”

“About what?” Sofia asked.

Rio shrugged, “Everything.”

“That’s a lot to think about,” Sofia said. She cocked her head to the side then asked, “Do you think aliens are real?”

The rest of dinner went by without any issues, followed by cake and singing and celebrations. Carla blew out her candles, stating loudly that she wished for more children in the family, and both Rio and Miguel, the two cousins left without children, pointedly avoided her stare. It was nearly midnight when everyone went to bed, but as she laid down to sleep, Rio found herself wide awake. Her earlier realization still buzzed within her mind, making her think of scenario after scenario where she might be able to tell Agatha her feelings.

After almost two hours of laying awake, Rio finally got up. She shrugged on a sweatshirt and padded down stairs to grab a glass of water.

Rio didn’t expect to find anyone else awake at this hour, but to her surprise, the back door was open. Walking closer, she found her father sitting outside on the porch swing, whiskey in one hand and cigarette in the other. Rio wrapped her arms around herself and joined him.

Luis kept the whiskey to himself, but he handed Rio the cigarette as soon as she sat down. 

Rio still remembered the first time her father caught her smoking. She was already twenty-one and in college, visiting home over winter break. The stress of being back around family was too much for her though, so she’d slipped out into the backyard for a smoke. When Luis found her, he merely sighed and smiled begrudgingly, asking if she had another for him.

After a while, Luis held his hand out. Rio handed the cigarette back and watched him take another drag. With smoke curling from his mouth, Luis said, “We haven’t spoken in months. We used to talk more.”

“You’re busy,” Rio said, but it was clear that even she didn’t think much of the excuse.

“Ah, but that’s no excuse,” Luis said with a knowing look. He reached out and squeezed her knee. “I’ve missed you.”

Rio felt her smile waver as she said, “I’ve missed you too, papi.”

Luis smiled at that. In an effort to make Rio proficient in English, they stopped speaking Spanish to her when she was very young. She also wasn’t allowed to speak Spanish, but every so often, the habit would come back in small ways. Despite being the one to suggest the rule, Luis was also the one who indulged Rio more when she messed up.

“You look tired,” Luis commented.

Rio sighed, “I am tired.”

“You look unhappy,” Luis added, making Rio tense. He smiled knowingly and nudged her. “You can say it,” he said. “I don’t expect things to be perfect with you and James immediately.”

Rio frowned and stared out at the backyard. She wished she could go back in time to when she was ten, when her biggest concern was making the boys let her play soccer with them. Rio sighed again and rubbed her hands over her thighs. 

“What if it’s never perfect?” Rio asked softly. “What if we’re never happy?”

“It hasn’t even been a year yet,” Luis replied. “Give it time.” He wrapped an arm around Rio now, hugging her to him. He kissed the side of her head and said, “I hope you can find happiness, no matter what happens.”

“Even if I never love James?” Rio hadn’t meant to say that, but it was too late. She felt her father tense against her. She held her breath, waiting for his response.

The two of them sat in silence for several long moments before Luis finally said, a pained finality to his words, “I want you to be happy. Just… within reason, Rio.”

Rio inhaled deeply, trying to will away the tears that gathered in her eyes. It was what she expected, so why did it still hurt so much to hear?

Rio stumbled to her feet, ignoring her father calling after her. She ran up to her room and locked the door, feeling like a little kid again. She leaned against the door, sucking in shuddering breaths. Rio blinked hard as the tears finally fell. She slid down the door until she sat curled against it. She buried her face in her arms, trying to muffle her cries.

A part of Rio, some naive, stupid part of herself, had hoped that her parents would be okay with the decision that had been brewing inside her mind over the last few weeks, but she knew now that they wouldn’t ever accept her after this. If Rio did this, she’d lose them, but wasn’t it already like she’d lost them? Rio rarely ever saw them anymore, and when she did, it was only ever about her marriage to James, never Rio herself.

Wiping her tears away, Rio grabbed her duffel off the floor and started packing up her stuff. She couldn’t stay here, not after that. Not after realizing that she still wanted Agatha, even knowing her father wouldn’t love her anymore for it. The back-to-back realizations made it impossible for Rio to just stay here and act like everything was okay.

The string that kept Rio tethered to her family had finally snapped.

Rio hoped the rest of her family would understand. Maybe not Victor, but maybe Miguel and Gabriel. God, she hoped Sofia would still be allowed to talk to her after this. 

Swallowing roughly, Rio slung her bag over her shoulder and headed straight out the door.

The car she ordered came within minutes, and as soon as she was inside, Rio changed her plans to a red-eye flight. Undoubtedly, when she landed, Rio would be flooded by calls and texts from her family, but she couldn’t bring herself to care anymore. She was done caring.

By the time Rio got on the flight, she was exhausted from the emotional toll the last day had been. She fell asleep quickly and deeply, and she didn’t wake up until a flight attendant shook her shoulder.

Rubbing her eyes, Rio squinted at the rising sun and checked the time. It was already eight in the morning. She ignored the thirty missed calls and eighty text messages. She turned off her phone and walked to the nearest subway that would take her home. 

Trudging up the stairs, Rio couldn’t wait to be alone in the apartment. She’d shower then sleep for a few more hours before she figured out what she was going to say to James. She had no idea how she was even going to broach the subject, but they’d already agreed to talk when she got back. She was finally going to tell him.

That was Rio’s plan when she went to unlock her door, only for it to swing open and reveal Agatha on the other side.

Chapter 19

Chapter Summary

“I’m a lesbian,” Rio blurted out. She couldn’t sit back and listen to James give the same speech he always did when Rio said this. There was never going to be a someday for them, and he needed to understand that.

Chapter Notes

this is a chapter that’s very dear to me and one i have been eager to write and share from the beginning

i hope you enjoy :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio blinked a few more times. Was she dreaming? She rubbed her eyes, but no, Agatha was still there, staring at her with just as much shock. 

“What,” Rio said, unsure of what she wanted to ask. She licked her lips.  Easiest question first. “What are you doing here?”

“Paperwork for Nicky. What are you doing here?” Agatha asked back. She held the door in a vice grip. “Aren’t you supposed to be in Texas?”

“Took an early flight back,” Rio said. She took a step forward then hesitated. “Agatha, what are you doing here?” She took another step closer, bringing her close enough that she could touch Agatha if she wanted. “Are you– Can we–” Rio took a deep breath, trying to gather her thoughts. “I need to talk to you.”

Agatha stared at her with wide eyes, trying to puzzle her out.

“Please,” Rio said. “I’m sorry. I’m so sorry about everything, but I’m ready now.” She reached out and grabbed Agatha’s hand, nearly crying when she didn’t pull away. Maybe she hadn’t ruined things completely. She took a shaky breath and said, “I’m ready. I want to talk to James and–”

“Talk to me about what?”

Rio snapped her mouth shut, body stiffening so suddenly that she felt her heart lurch into her throat. She let go of Agatha’s hand and watched as James stepped out from around the corner, looking at her curiously. He was dressed for work with an undone tie hanging around his neck. Agatha must have caught him right before he left.

“Ready for what?” James asked. He glanced between the two of them and continued, “Wait, what are you doing home already? Your flight wasn’t supposed to land until tonight.” He stepped up beside Agatha. “What’s going on?”

“I took an earlier flight,” Rio repeated, looking between James and Agatha. Her mouth felt dry. Her head began to spin. This was not how she intended to do this at all. “I got into a fight with my dad.”

Realization dawned on Agatha’s face while James furrowed his brows, asking, “About what?” He shook his head and stepped back. “What are we doing, talking about this in the hall? Come on.” He took a few steps then looked at Agatha. “Are you staying?”

“Should I?” Agatha asked, but she wasn’t looking at James. She was looking at Rio. 

Rio nodded and said quietly, “Please.”

James looked at them, and Rio could see his mind trying to understand what was happening. After a moment, he just turned and kept going to the living room. When he was far enough away, Rio stepped closer and said, “I’m going to tell him everything.”

“Everything?” Agatha repeated with a raised brow. “Are you sure about that?”

“Yes,” Rio said without hesitation. “If that’s okay with you.”

Agatha’s face softened, something like hope in her eyes. She nodded and brushed her hand against Rio’s. “Okay,” she said softly. “If you’re sure.”

“Thank you,” Rio murmured. “And I swear we can talk about everything later, starting with a thousand apologies from me.”

“I’ll hold you to that,” Agatha said, and the smile wasn’t quite the same as the one from before, but it was closer than anything Rio could have hoped for. “Come on.”

When they walked into the living room, they found James already sitting in one of the arm chairs. Rio swallowed and took a seat on the couch, relieved when Agatha sat down next to her. It certainly didn’t help the increasingly irritated, confused look on James’s face, but Rio felt better with Agatha’s support so tangible.

Rio folded her hands in her lap and took a deep breath. She began, speaking carefully, “James, you know I said I wasn’t in love with you, that I wasn’t sure if I’d ever be in love with you.”

“Yes, I know, Rio,” James said with a wave of his hand, “but I’m patient. I can–”

“I’m a lesbian,” Rio blurted out. She couldn’t sit back and listen to James give the same speech he always did when Rio said this. There was never going to be a someday for them, and he needed to understand that. Rio chanced a look at James’s face, finding it frozen in shock. Her heart thumped hard in her chest as she continued, “I never told my parents, so they set me up with you and–”

“And you married me anyways?” James cut her off. His tone was expectedly upset, but Rio still felt awful at how distraught he sounded.  “Knowing you’d never be able to love me?”

“There was no guarantee I’d ever love you, even if I was straight,” Rio tried to reason.

James just shook his head and said, “That’s different.”

Rio wasn’t sure it was, but she just took another deep breath and said, “There’s more.”

“More?” James said.

Rio hesitated and glanced at Agatha. 

James saw this and laughed bitterly, “What, Agatha knew you were into women before me?”

Rio bit her lip. She cleared her throat and said, “In a way, yes.”

“What do you mean, ‘in a way’?” James said.

“Well,” Rio began, but the rest never came. She thought she’d have more time. She thought she’d have an opportunity to word this as nicely as possibly, so it wouldn’t hurt so much. All the ways to say this rang in Rio’s head, but she couldn’t bring herself to actually say them out loud. Rio looked to Agatha again, brown eyes wide with desperation. Agatha sighed.

“We slept together, James,” Agatha finally said, losing patience. “Several times, at the beginning of your marriage. Rio ended things after a few months because she couldn’t handle the guilt. Nothing’s happened since then.”

James looked like he’d been struck. He blinked dazedly before he stood up. “Months?” James said under his breath. He began to pace wildly, dragging his hands over his face 

Agatha bit her lip and said, “James–”

James held up a hand, and to Rio’s surprise, Agatha stopped. “This can’t be happening,” James said, a hint of hysteria entering his voice. “I’m not an idiot. I would have known if Rio was cheating. I would have known if it was with you!”

Rio could see the way Agatha seemed to be physically restraining herself from pointing out that he didn't know though.

“I thought this was about losing a friend!” James exclaimed. “Not, not–” He looked at Agatha, his face full of poison. “I can’t believe you.” He looked at Rio now, and where there’d been a kind of resignation with Agatha, there was nothing but betrayal for Rio. “And you. Was it all a lie then? Every time you were nice? Every time you listened to me complain about work or family? Was it just you keeping me happy so you could fuck my sister?”

Rio deserved it, but she still shut her eyes at the accusation. When she opened them again, both James and Agatha were on their feet.

“Watch your mouth,” Agatha hissed. 

“Stay out of this,” James snapped. “Thanks to you my marriage is over.” He tried to walk away.

“You don’t even love her!” Agatha shouted. She stepped in front of him before he could leave the living room. “What right do you have to be upset?”

“What right?” James laughed, but it was strangled and furious and cruel. “I think I have every right to be upset that my wife and my sister were fucking behind my back!” He ran a hand through his hair, and Rio felt her heart stutter at how much like Agatha he looked with just one simple move. “You’re not supposed to fuck your brother’s wife,” James said before lowering his voice and adding, “I thought you had at least that much decency.”

“Don’t do that,” Agatha said, voice trembling. She pointed an accusing finger at James. “Don’t act like this is all my fault.”

“Isn’t it?” James snapped. He stepped into her space so that her finger was pressed hard against his chest. “You always ruin everything!”

“You always get everything!” Agatha screamed. 

A deafening silence followed, and although Rio was acutely aware of the way Agatha shook with barely contained rage, she also couldn’t look away from James’s expression, anger and confusion melding together. Did he never realize how deep Agatha’s own resentment ran?

“You always get everything,” Agatha repeated, her voice cracking on the last word. Her hand curled into a fist that rested against his chest. “The oldest, the boy, the perfect child that our parents always wanted.”

“I didn’t ask for any of that,” James argued.

Agatha laughed hollowly, “But you got it all anyways, didn’t you?” To this, James had no response. “How do you think it felt growing up? I was the spare, and to make matters worse, I was a girl.”

“You didn’t make things any easier for yourself by acting out,” James said.

“And where would that have gotten me?” Agatha said. “Married off to the highest bidder?” As soon as the words left her mouth, Rio flinched. Agatha wasn’t even looking at her, but she still spun around, eyes wide. “Wait, Rio. I didn’t mean–”

“We’ll talk about it later,” Rio said quietly. She stood up and met James’s gaze evenly. She said, “Don’t blame her for everything, James. She didn’t make me do anything I didn’t want to.”

“This is what she does, Rio,” James insisted. “I told you that. She always has to break the rules. It doesn’t matter who gets hurt as a result.”

The way James spoke so callously about Agatha sent a wave of fury through Rio. “Don’t talk about other people getting hurt when you’ve never given a damn when your parents hurt Agatha,” Rio snapped.

“What the hell are you talking about?” James said, shaking his head a little as if to wave the notion off.

Chapter 22

Chapter Summary

It hurt more to be back here than she imagined. It wasn’t just the suffocating pressure to be the perfect wife that lived here. It was also the quiet understanding of two people doing their best to please their parents. It was the tentative friendship of a husband and wife, only in name. It was Rio, or at least a piece of her.

Chapter Summary

The fragile happiness Rio found came crashing down three days later.

The fragile happiness Rio found came crashing down three days later.

Before it happened though, Rio got to experience true domestic bliss, and despite what would happen after, she wouldn’t have traded it for anything in the world. It filled Rio with a wondrous kind of happiness that also ached deep in her chest.

WIFE SWAP:
Senator Vidal’s Daughter Trades Senator Harkness For His Own Sister

Accompanying the article was a photo of Rio and Agatha kissing in the car in front of her old apartment, the one she shared with James. 

Rio felt her stomach clinch at the headline. Her thumb hovered over the link, but she couldn’t bring herself to actually click it and read what was said. This was everywhere. Everyone would see it, including her parents, who she hadn’t worked up the nerve to speak to yet. Rio was going to throw up.

What made those days even better though was always ending them with Agatha and Nicky. As life went on, there were nights where Rio only saw Agatha or Nicky for dinner, instead of both; Agatha would have a late meeting or Nicky was out with friends, but it still felt special to share any meal with them. If Agatha was gone, Rio and Nicky would watch a horror film she’d hate. If Nicky was gone, Rio and Agatha would take full advantage of having an empty house.

On days like those, Rio felt like nothing could ever go wrong.

However, there were days where Rio felt herself crumple under the realization that she’d lost her family. It happened around Mother’s Day and again when it was Luis’s birthday. Although she sent texts and made calls on both days, all went unanswered. She’d expected it, but it still felt like a gaping hole inside of her. Rio mourned the loss by withdrawing and falling silent. When it had happened, Agatha had panicked, not that she would have admitted that. 

“Do you want me to stay home?” Agatha asked. She sat on the edge of the bed, running her finger through Rio’s hair. She was dressed for the day while Rio was still in her pajamas under the covers. “Say the word, and I’ll cancel my meetings.”

“No,” Rio mumbled. The ache in her chest felt like it would swallow her whole at any moment, and even speaking took tremendous effort. “Go to work.”

Agatha’s eyebrows furrowed. “Rio,” she said softly. “I don’t mind.” When Rio said nothing, pulling the covers up to her nose, Agatha sighed and said, “I’m taking the day off.”

She would tell him to do one thing, but he’d end up doing something else. She told herself Agatha wasn’t James, but she felt the deja vu nonetheless.
